Many times a sickness called "telul" is born at the joint of the hip, and it grows and becomes very large until it is a visible thing to look at; and for this reason you should cut it at the beginning, and all bone must be removed, then put on its place the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays in cutting it until it is large, he takes warning if it is hard, of dull color, of poor feeling: do not touch it with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, for when one cuts it any time, it brings great evil to the sick person; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of dull color, and you see that one can cut it all, then empty the sick person and cut it without fear, and cure the place with things drying and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the hip is cut and sewed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes in one of these worked cartilages, it profits little because in no men.  
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary when this happens to any one, if it is looked at that the wound is fresh in all its blood; and then adjust the two lips with a suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if the lips are already opened on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape all parts of their core until they heal, then assemble the two lips with a suture, and restrain them, and powder on top of dragon's blood powder, and ground incense; and put on the powders a piece of strong plasters or other soldering plaster, and let it stay until it falls off by itself, and then cure it with ointment until it is healed. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the stitch is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In men's mouths often happen within the lips abscesses hard, seeming like grains of mustard, and smaller and larger; therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut above each pustule, and take with tweezers and chop in each part; then apply to the place after incision of powdered vitriol, until the blood be stanched; and then the ointment of honey, and cure the place with dry things until it be healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times flesh grows on the gums, that the ancients call "albulus"; therefore it is necessary that you hold it with forceps, and cut it at its root, and leave to clot the wound or blood; then put on the place powdered vitriol, or other powders astringent and drying; and if that flesh returns after the incision, which happens often, so cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and harsh; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green as long as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are smelly; so it is necessary for you to make the patient sit between your hands, and his chin be in your saint, and remove the teeth or scabs that appear, until there remains nothing; and thus do of the blackness and the greening, and the jaundice and other spots, until they are cleansed; and if one removes those that are at the first reason, it is good; if those no, so it starts again to re-remove the second day and the third, until you have all removed; and know that the teeth need different forms of instruments for removal, according to what the work shows them, because the scraper used to remove outside teeth have other forms than those used between teeth; and these forms and others be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you wait for the drawing as much as you can, because one must not do it badly; because it is a substance very high until then one has no excuse to remove.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to treat, it behoves you to be certain of the tooth aching. 
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain of the patient, and believes it to be a tooth saint, and makes milk the good tooth; and nonetheless departs not the pain by this, as long as the evil is strained, for we have already done so to these saints; and when you are well certain of the tooth aching, then it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth with all i. spatumile strong to keep the gum from all parts; then move it to your two or tweezers subtle at the first point and point, as long as it is well loosened, then I affirm it well the pliers; and let the head of the patient in your saint between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After the tooth is extracted straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out fully, take one of these instruments and put it inside each side gently, and move it as you did first. 
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and broken, then it is necessary to fill it with sponges, where the holes are; and if you extract it carefully with tweezers, so that it does not break when extracting it; and it is necessary very skillfully to work around the gum in order to dislodge the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And therefore well guard that you do not break it, and remaining a part, and return to the patient by the malice of the root greater pains than the first. 
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take heed that you do not act as the ignorant physicians do, who through their haste and boldness sometimes break the cartilage, and bring them not what we have recounted; but bring forth sometimes by the opening of those great illnesses for the roots that remain there, or for the cartilage that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, wash its place with wine or oil and salt; and if a discharge of blood comes, which often happens, apply to the place vitriol ground; and if that does not work, cauterize it. 
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, to which one must use teeth first, be at long points and thick handles, that they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick members so that they do not bend when pulling, and be of well-made iron, and be toothed for gripping firmly.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in the breast, it is necessary that you put over it cotton moistened with butter for one or two days. 
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the eyes are moist, put in the tongs that are called “algefri,” so that the head seems like a bird's beak; and be made inside as much as a file and this is the form.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say a spatula, because of this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with this, it is good; if it does not, help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come after.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has two teeth, of which is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments that are in front in the direction of the teeth, and this instrument which seems like a large pair of pliers, whose shape is here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be so that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned; and the wise masters subtle find for themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are such diseases where the ancient ones do not teach any instrument for the diversity of others and if one does not break the bone or other bones, or it can, then search for the instruments that are needed, that I have told you, and help with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-fitting to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but it can hold and remove; and then restore its place with medicines suitable to this, and if there is in the bone rot, and it is small, then the king has all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to the natural body, and the shape is ugly, and even in virgin women, then it behooves you to know if the tooth is born after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot file it or file it; therefore the rake; and if it is attached with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is here, and is similar to .i. small beak, and let it be of sharp iron at its tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the coping bit by bit in hands for a few days because of the hardness of the tooth, and for those you do not move others, and if it appears that it can be filed, then the file of a piece like this is the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file used to make needles; and in filing the tooth bit by bit over a few days gently, so that it does not move until it falls; then the plane at the end without any ridge, and if the tooth is too sharp and it wounds the tongue, then it is necessary to file the roughness until it is equal, so that it does not wound the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth in front loosens, whether by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it so that he does not bite, and you have treated them with constricting medicines, and it is of no use; then it is necessary to restrain it with a gold thread, because the silver thread becomes green and rotten, but gold never changes; and be the thread medium, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see fit to bring together the teeth, then take the thread and put it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the cheek between the teeth, if there is one or more, until you come sagely to the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin again the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and wisely, so that it does not move; and be your ligation at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. 
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the bones of the jaw with pliers and assemble them, and place them between the healthy teeth, and place it so that it does not touch the tongue; and then leave it tight as much as it can remain, and if it unties, or the wires come loose, restrain it with another wire; thus it remains and serves for its entire time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the adjustment of the two healthy teeth, and the two bad ones, as you see: 
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, then one puts it back in its place, from fresh to fresh, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and suffering, and at any time one makes the shape of a tooth from the bone of a calf, and one puts it in the place where the lack is, and one restrains it as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No times is this ligature that comes from under the tongue or nature, that one is born thus; or by accident of a joined wound; and the works are such that you work the mouth of the sick person, and have his head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous tie wide, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its holding, and if there is hardness or knot, and it is from the joining of a wound, so put the probe and cut wide that ligament; and keep that the cutting be not too deep, for the artery which is below; and when you have done, then lift the place with rose water and oil, or cold water, then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and stitch the sick person each night, that the places may not close. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the flow of blood comes, then place on the place powdered vitriol; and if the bleeding does not stop, then cauterize it with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.  
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of fiery color or black or hard, so that the sick person does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining to whiteness, and there is moisture, then place the probe, and make it with a subtle spatula, and deliver it on one side and the other; and if the blood does not stop at your work, put on top vitriol ground until it is extinguished, then return to your work until you draw everything out; then raise the level of assil and seil, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there come from within the throat lumps which are called «godath», and they call them properly the II almonds, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, if you take care: if it is abscesses hard of little sense and color, do not touch them with iron. 
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for the discharge of blood; but leave it until it is mature, and then you will split it, or it would break by itself; and if it is of white color, appear the instrument to cover, but first see if the abscess boils and rests. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore make the patient sit before the sun, and his hips be in good health, and he open his mouth and the surgeon places the instruments between his hands, and presses the tongue down with all the instrument, for this is the form; and be it of silver or steel as well as a knife: 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And you press the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the oncine and stick it in the almond, and drive it upward more than you can; and do nothing of the cloths with, then cut with the instrument, from this is the form, that seems a forces; and anyway the chief are curved, and one place the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron inde or d’andainne:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, cut it with pliers, from this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be trenching on one side, and on the other part name; and when you have cut one of the almonds, so cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water and ease, and if there is a discharge of blood, gargle the patient with water, or grated pomegranate peels, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the wound is cleansed; then treat it until it is healed; and at no time when other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two almonds, so cut them like the two almonds always.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman of an abscess that was within her throat, that is to say the abscess of little size; and I had well almost closed the whole throat, so that the woman could not expire by the conduit which was stopped, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained thus one day or two. 
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had to be opened two times through the two openings of the veins. 
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore did so, and put it in one incision, then the traitor was taken out, and there was a large portion of bowel removed; then I made another piece on the other side of the two incisions, and I worked the mouth and pressed his tongue; after which I put the incision into these abscesses, and in coped a part, and no more than a little blood came out; and thus the conduits of the throat were opened for the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut that abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I engulfed it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained without growing; and I left those parts, and I know only what God did to her after me. 
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it comes back to the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is somewhat thick and round, it is called "eye". 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the chausses abscess is calmed, and it is subtle, then it behooves you to cut it; and the one that is rounded assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of fusse color or black, then it behooves you to eschew the incision of it. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril to the patient. 
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, by its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit facing the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we have made remembrance before; then insert the needle into the grape, and draw it down, and the cup on one of the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds. 
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural term; for if you cut more, you harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears to have it cut, then you must use an instrument to cauterize the senses that cause fear. 
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp, acute. 
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head on your healthy one, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said in this chapter of cautery, and confides with lively water, so that it be neither too thick nor too clear; and by employing the end of this instrument, for this purpose is the form: 
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let him have his head a hair or one puts the medicine in it, as the men of a spoon, and put the instrument to all the medicine on the grape; and the patient be lying on his side, so that the saliva and the muscles run from his mouth of the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the back; then hold your hand to all the medicine and press it on the grape, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it curdle and the bites of the medicine be appeased; and if you see, take cotton and surround it with any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument to all the cotton in the cane above, until the cotton hardens on the grape; and do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and fall after four or five days. And if you have need to recommence the cautery of the medicine, then commence it again, and after the cautery wipe around the grape, with cotton wrapped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and be cured with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, or the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take wormwood and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and lavender and similar herbs, and assemble all of them or any of them in one pot, and put them therein, and let boil; and the pot should be well glued with strong earth, and within the pot have one instrument shaped as follows:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether it be of silver or of iron, and let one of the heads be put in the mouth of the sick person until the vapor rises to the uva by the vein, until the uva is mortified; after that begin again, as long as the uva dries, and keep that you do not make this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, for many things happen; and do not make this except at the declination of the hot abscess. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a dog and put inside its head a wick of wool, so that the mouth of the patient does not become too hot; because the wick of wool does not allow the vapor to burn the mouth, and it is a good cure together with salvation. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or spine of fish, or something else, lodges in the throat; so it is therefore necessary that you pull out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with the whole instrument, so that you may move the thing; and what does not appear to you and is returned into the throat, it is necessary that you make the sick person vomit as long as the food is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it will throw out the thing airy by vomiting; or the sick person swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or one morsel of dry bread; and tie to the sponge one thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to its place, it will lodge itself, and then you will pull it out; and if it does not come out by what we have said, then take one instrument of plank according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all come into it, nor thrust in the bone; and it is better that the patient thrusts the instrument, because he knows whether the thing is harsh; if he pushes down, or he pulls up all of the instrument equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the bleeding of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes medicine is used for the bloodletting, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the patient to the sun, then that you press the tongue with the instrument that I have told you. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the hernia, then treat it with all small tweezers, or subtle forceps that are good for this. 
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this is not good, then take a dog's hair and put it in the throat of the patient, then put where the end of the dog's hair was on fire, and do this often.  
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient stands in water all day. 
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full the cup of cold water, and open the mouth, and lay it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the patient feels the water, he will fall.  
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then smoke the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times because it will certainly cure. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot or it has burning charcoal, and be the bottom covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and in that pierce the head of the instrument; then throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cauldron in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not go out, but comes to the nose; and the nose will now run, and if it does not run, you begin the fumigation again many times; and suffer the patient thirst, and spits things salty and such, and do not drink water; and then the matter is necessary that it must come out by this governance. 
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument for treating the root is, when it can be seen, like tongs bent to enter the throat; and has the appearance of a bird's beak, and has sharpness from lime, so that when it takes hold, it cannot let go; and see here the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what the remembrance comes after in this book, and they are diverse in puncture and size; and this is in two ways, one being in its same form, and of that which it holds moisture.  
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the joints which are in the body. 
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess of the head is other than that of the foundation, and the abscess of the flesh is other than that which comes in the joints, and each one has its judgment in the work. 
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if on abscesses one should not probe, as long as the boil is mature according to its accomplishment; and if on some such ones that it is necessary to probe when they are ripe, and do not die according to their accomplishment, such as abscesses which are near joints. 
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near the joints, and it is left as long as it is corrupted, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint are putrid, so this is the cause of contraction in that limb. 
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal member; if it is near the foundation, then pierce it so that it is ripe; and it is not necessary that you pierce an abscess crudely without completed digestion, except for the one which is near the foundation, lest it be too deep, and become lengthened inside, and there comes a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time. 
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of the perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to its completion, and it is when the pain is appeased, and the fever subsides, and the lessening of the pain and the redness, and the suppuration and the softening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where it depends most from the abscess, and where it appears to open more; and be the perforation long in the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equal where there is no pleurisy.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these things that are broken, according to that member.  
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is good that you let the perforation remain until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. 
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before these, the body of the venom will be extended from it, and it is full of much filth; and by chance harden the lips and depths of it.  
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess that are felt according to the width of the body, according to what the members have need. 
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you bring in small abscesses, small punctures; and in large abscesses, large punctures, and many incisions according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to shave the heart, and cover; when it has become as I draped, and is softened, then it is necessary to do as one does with buboes: and if there are such that are cut in III angles, and if there are such that one copes like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the angres; and if there are such where one makes a round size, and other sizes and seeming cuts. 
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	He who has no chief, as a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce him plainly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, if do not milk all the pus in that hour, but drain one part; then stop the abscess until the next day, then drain nothing straight; make this many times of great to great, until the pus is all out; same as if the patient is of feeble virtue, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old men decrepit. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes trembles with the exit of the bowels, which by chance kills the patient, and you don't worry about it. 
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, then wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a flat incision, administer pads of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then it is necessary that you put in each one a pad so that they come together; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, and you have sewn it together, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or lint scraped from linen without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then bone, and cure with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, so administer cold water and ease it, and moisten the bandage, and put on the bleeding site many times. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, administer government and care, and the powders that I have said in this book, and if it is in winter, and the place or abscesses is very nervous, then it behooves you to put upon tents and drapes moist with wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the place is fleshy, then it behooves you to put on moist drapes in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, up to the third day, as we have said; and then untie the abscess and wipe it and cure it, as it behooves, until it is healed. 
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this it is necessary to know universally in cures of abscesses: or I have said how one must go before the cures of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where near the head come small abscesses, and are mannered as we that are in cloths, as well as the trellis of a vine, and much in them there are similarities.  
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and such which have moisture as well as poultices; and there are some that are hard and stony at the waist, and there is no doubt if the artery does not go against it. 
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the waist is that you prove all the instrument which is called "entromissoire," from which its form comes after, what thing it contains. 
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then raise it upward by its length. 
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, so scrape with nothing leaving the hair that contains that moisture, because it returns to where it was when you leave it alone; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and honey, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who have this remaining will cure.  
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then he begins the cotton again, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain in any dirt; then cure the wound with ointment suitable to it, until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds in the fat, then cut according to this form, long; and put your tweezers there, and the skin around it, and put all your care into draining further the coat where it lies; and if the artery does contrary, then do what I have told you after. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same with an abscess if it is foul, and of its size and of its care as I have told you. 
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the tail on a pus abscess and the moist one is lighter because they have little blood. 
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if in any of these abscesses or chief where there is no moisture, and of these abscesses that I treated or chief of an old woman; and I found the abscess as a hard stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if one had tried to make any incision, one would have made him a wound as well as from a stone. 
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or chief, for that which come at the chief of children and at the roots of ears, the opening so be all days to the most dependent place, for to let out the pus; and the cure as it is fitting. 
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses happen at the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come from other parts of the body, and they are bad, and they are intertwined with each other. 
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its side, like the boils and abscesses of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulas are many. 
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some who contain moisture, and there are some who do not want to obey health.  
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	in that one then that you see of good disposition at the touching, and is similar to the color of the body, and moves from each part and is not hard to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the conduit, and is not deep; so it is necessary that you cut it above, and the scrape of each part, and are the II lips of the heart as incisions, if you have need for it, as we have said in abscesses of the chief; and the trade prick and prick, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and do not be the spatula thick or trenching, that the hands escape, and see too forward, that you do not cut what you do not.  
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it will not stop bleeding, put in the wound ground vitriol, or some powders that restrain blood, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscesses are calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.  
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is cleansed, return to your work, until you complete it; then if there remain any small scabs on your fingertip, cut them and remove them. 
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if it has in the root of the scrofulous vein a great one, then it does not behoove that you cut that scrophula at its root, but bind it with a strong double thread, and let it hang by it, without annoyance; then apply the wound of old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then cure. 
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, since there is no remaining superfluity for the size of the scrofula.  
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and milk it out, and use it as we have said. 
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that hold superfluity, pierce there where it opens more; and pierce thus as the one before said, depending, then administer tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what is remaining of corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply the ointment cure to create flesh, until it is healed.  
de squinance	of a swelling
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen in our land who made it, and this is the scripture of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinancy, it is necessary that the slit of the throat which is called 'epiglottis' be evacuated; and do not help them by this, because all the veins and arteries of the sick are hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in two cheeks.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the artery, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three circles or four a small cut through, between the two circles or by the quantity of the cut through the syfac, not in the cartilage; and this their si is convenient to the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long.  
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it behooves him to extend the skin of the throat to all the hinge, then split the heart as long as it comes to the channel; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the syfac, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the channel that it goes out through the place which is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open a piece. 
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed of which one doubts strangulation, assemble the .ij. lips of the wound of the heart, and sew entirely alone sense the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one should not do this juice until the throat is completely choked, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the fault belongs to the wing.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, cover the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and they breathe through the wound, and thus are saved from death; and for this reason the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the illness has passed, and it has passed in III days or in IIII. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, as long as it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took the knife and stabbed it in her throat, and cut part of the channels of the windpipe; and I was called by her to heal her, and I found her as dead. 
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood which was issuing from it, and well that it had not pierced a vein nor been conducted further than the throat, and the veins were issued through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I bandaged it, and thus I treated the wound, and healed it until it was well; and did not happen to the girl except that she was hoarse of voice, and returned afterwards to her disposition; for this reason I say that in cutting the epiglottis there should be no fear. 
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "throat hernia", and it is a large abscess in the color of a boil, and it is mostly in women; and it is according to II manners: natural, and accidental; where naturally has no engine. 
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is according to II manners, of which one is similar to fat for us, and the other manner is similar to abscess that comes from our artery; and there is fear, and it does not become to work to do fiercely except in this one that is small, and proves and searches all the intruder: if you find him as I fat, and cannot at any vein, so chop him, as one chops the fat, and treat him all his scalp, if there is any; and encircles well soon, and cures him as it befits, until he is perfectly sound.  
des nous	Of ours
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways of us are, which I will say all the resemblances; and now it is fitting that I say all the difference that is between our and issue. 
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is sometimes feverish and hot-bearing, as long as the boiling is not passed, and is completed the rotting; therefore rest fever and heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new flesh there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains the cyst, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins as a wound, and becomes swollen; and there are according to two appearances, or greasy, or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division. 
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the new [wound], that you feel and examine first with all the instrument that is called "entromissoire", according to what its form will come or chapter which is afterwards.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses for us is that you prick or more moist place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two thumbs and thumbs, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then it shall be according to the size of the abscess; then extract the entromissoire, and take care in those that jump out. 
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the moisture runs short, what color it is, do it as I have said of other abscesses; and if after the probe moisture does not come, know that it is fatty, so do it in a cross, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape each side and ward the coat where it lies so that you draw it out healthy with the probe; and if you cannot draw it out healthy, so draw it by pieces so that nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it remains there nothing, it returns to us many times; and if it remains a little, and the wound doesn't grieve you, apply to the wound some corrosive powders, sharp, and restrain the wound, and put above calming things, hot poultice, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the lump is great, sew the two lips of the wound, and cure it from what generates flesh.   
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is bleeding heavily or otherwise quickly, and you are in haste, apply a mixture of crushed vitriol, and let it lie for two or three days, until the wound dries, and calms the flow of blood; then return to covering what remains.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the intrumental probes, and they are in 3 manners: large and medium and small; and there are 3 squares which are called “albaret,” and 1 that is called “breb,” and there are also in 3 manners: large, medium, and small, to surround the abscesses of fistula; and they are also like needles with which one sews sorceresses, and are of citrine gold, or iron, or silver, and the most valuable are those which are yellow, and they are more proved of black flint to surround the fistulas of curvature; and they are in 3 manners: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the breadth of the openings.  
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the pincers are of many resemblances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are pincers that have two curves in three ways also; and there are pincers that have three curves, and they are also in three ways; and there are pincers that have two curves, and pincers of a single curve only, and they are in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these things is that one makes them sharp, and there are some that do not cut more than one side, with which one skins the veins, for that one does not cut the vein or the nerve; and of these intromissories are the alemeles put back in handles, so that the patient does not feel them when opening abscesses; and they are three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them only in fleshy places, like legs, arms, nipples, and groin, and similar ones; and sometimes one makes another instrument small, resembling fisticuffs, according to this form, with which one stops bleeding.  
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And one puts it at times in the place which heals with a cutting of veins, and arteries, and at times returns according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they seem like the breasts of a woman; and they remain disfigured and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them, it is necessary to follow according to this form from this line .b. up to .g.:  
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound preventing flesh, then assemble the two lips of the wound with stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if the swelling is low, and softened like it happens to women, so make it in two ribs above, by two similar incisions; so that one holds to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. until the line .g.; then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and put therein what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood loss, then you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it softens the remaining and fat, then cure it until it is healed. 
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the buttocks are kinds of hard scrofulous boils or nodules and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those therefore who contain moisture ought to be cut according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g.:
