Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then apply the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and care of ointment before that as long as it is healing.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of a resemblance to scrofula, then treat it as we have said in incisions of scrofulas, and if the wound returns pus, then administer cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is wounded, and the skin is sewn which is above, there often comes abscesses, and it also happens to the vein inflamed and abscess; and if the one knows this way that it is for the artery, so the abscess long is made by him; and when you feel it in your fingers, you feel a tightness; and when it is for the vein, then it is red appearing outside; and it is folly to cover this abscess, even when it is below the armpits and arms and neck and in many other places, and is very large. 
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to avoid the cure of iron, and whoever is at the head it is also necessary to avoid it, and in the one who is inflamed with artery by above the skin of the long; then work the waist as soon as possible, and depart beautifully the artery from the fabrics, until it is discovered; then put under it a needle, and make it pierce up to the other side, and extract the artery of a double thread in II leagues, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the II arteries that are in the temples; then point the place which is between the II ties of an intromissoire until the blood comes out of it, and be relieved the abscess; then administer the cure that causes bowe, as long as the tie sticks; then cure those who have ointment before these, until it is healed; and if the abscess is for the size of the vein, then it is necessary that you hold in your hand what you can of the abscess to all the skin, then put the needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and there is the double thread, so that you draw it from the other side; then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or tie of one of II parts as II chiés of the thread; and if you doubt that the threads are not issued, then put another needle to all the thread under all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and extract the threads in IIII leagues; then cut the abscess until the superfluities come out of it, then cut the superfluity of the keur and leave what is tied; then put on top I drapeil moilliet in wine and oil, then administer them cures of tents and ointments until it is healed. 
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also as abscesses come in the artery and in the vein, abscesses come in the nerves when they are overworked, or by too much labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and hips and in all the places where there are joints, and it is a grief abscesses, and its color seems like the color of the body, and is in many dispositions without pain; and when one restrains them forcibly, the patient feels pain, and is not at all in harmony with the body, but below the heart; and moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor down or up, and the one who is in the joints should not be covered with iron: for fear it would go contraction; and the one who is on the head or forehead, makes the skin to the spatula. 
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it with a string, and then scrape it, then pick it up and sew the wound together with stitches, and care for it until it is healed. 
des grosses boces pendans	of large abscesses hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the belly and nowhere else; and it is a disease that is called “fungus” because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and the roots are subtle, and the head is large; and there are small ones and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his belly which were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and they had fine roots, and they were slightly split, and moisture oozed from them. 
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI З., and the work in the incision is that you watch if the patient is moist, and the color of the little artery is white and moist and of subtle root; if the chop at the spatula wide, and be in your presence the cautery to fire. 
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the waist often comes too great a bleeding, and if it does not go well, then hasten therefore to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision of iron, then take the thread of lead well made, and bind the artery as we have said, and leave it for days; and then restrain it, and do not cease to restrain the lead thread until it cuts the artery, and bleeds through it without working; and if the roots are large, you are afraid to cut even the same for the belly, but you may well cut half, then cauterize that it does not return; then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cut the flesh which is of a pale color and poor in sense and milk. 
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	Because it is an abscess festering, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the wound is healed
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the abscess comes from cautery of a wound or fissure of the skin, and it is on the belly and in some of the bowels, as it happens in other wounds, or of blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or of wind; and if it is through the rupture of the skin and the exit of the pus, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open of diverse issues. 
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when it is pressed to its sides, it rises back up, and then returns, and by chance, it may be tightened, and enlarges much at the entrance of the bath and for hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it; and if it is due to blood, it opens by these signs the abscesses large and hard, and is bound according to a quantity; and if it is due to wind, it is sore to the touch, and the works are that you look at its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or vein, or wind. 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary that you leave the care.  
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in this chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein. 
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the boil, then it befits that you command the patient to hold his arm, and let it be stretched straight, then reign in around the bulge; then command him to gesir sovin between your hands, then go around the place that you have signed to all the spatula, then extend the half of the abscess above to the whole great uncine; then tie it around with a strong thread, or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let the two ends be tied on each other; then operate the half of the abscess extended on the thread, and put your index finger in, and search the intestine; if you find it taken by the thread, then untie it, and put the intestine outside of the belly; and if you find the boil, take it at the uncine, and cut off the superfluity; and if the artery makes it contrary, or the vein, then go well around, then return to your work and take II needles, and put II through threads, and put the II needles around what you have done in a cross that you make perceable; then strain the abscess in IV lengths on the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place as long as it will rot, and let the dead flesh fall away by itself; or you cut it when it is subtle and rotting, then cure it of what is necessary, and shave the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or the moisture that you find, then cure the place of what is necessary, and close the place. 
dou chancre	about the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of ulcers, and how one should work on them with medicines, and how one should avoid the cure of iron; and let us say that ulcers are created in the marshes, and great caution is needed in their treatment, and ancients said that when an ulcer is in a place where it can be scraped like an ulcer that is in the nipples, and in the groin, and similar places, and it should be completely removed when it is at its beginning; and when it is large and old, it is not appropriate that you approach it, because I have never healed any of them; nor has anyone else ever healed any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient once of black bile; then make him bleed if he has a manifest repletion, then prepare the patient's skin well to perform the operation; then cut out your ulcer or sore, and shave it all around, and remove it from all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood flow freely, and press the place firmly with your hand or any other thing, and if the flow of blood goes against the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the bleeding is stopped; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: so is revealed only; and one should not touch iron in these II similarities: that is to know, tympanites and hydrops, because it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this semblance of dropsy which is called “eclites” of medicines, and the cure does not profit, consider if the sick person is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and diarrhea and similar things; if you do not touch iron because there is doubt; and if you see the sick person of strong virtue, and he has no other illness but dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must thus work: lift the sick person right up on your hands, and the minister presses the belly pushing the water to the lowest part of the hip, then take the spatula spiny according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be cut from two parts. 
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	At the point, and nevertheless it should not be so deep that it can come to the intestine when you put it in, and you cannot bleach it; then look if the dropsy is engendered towards the intestines: if it is necessary that you fenestrate under the head III of two right below the armpit; and if the dropsy is for the disease of the liver, so be your incision to the left of the head III of two; and if it is for the spleen, so be it to the right, and it should not happen that the patient lies on the incision so that the superfluities do not run to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and the outlet, and raise your hand to the entire spatula between the skin and the syfac as in scraping to the quantity of a fingernail or like an inch; then pierce the syfac until the spatula comes to the point eight, and this is the place of the water, then the treatment drive, and put this instrument for this reason:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a silver needle, and it is made of iron or lead light, and at the bottom part there is I small hole; and on one side it costs III holes; and II on the other side, and I on the other; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the form of the incision with which the scribes cut the feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the chief above is the alemele, so that when the instruments comes to the point, it descends now on the instrument; empty therefore half or a third part, for if you empty more than it is fitting in that hour, by adventure the patient may die for the resolution of his spirit from the arm, or he falls faint, or he approaches to death; but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulses; then treat the instrument and retain the point, and it is retained now by the heart which stops the leak which is on the siphon, for this that I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then begin again the instrument the other day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and treat from the point a little quantity; do this any day, and keep yourself from following until there remains not more than a bit of point. 
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt on the patient, and give him much water, so cure him with a burial or hot sand, and by much sweat or bath and in the sun, and keep him from drinking; and cure him with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stoppage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	At no time are children born who do not have a hole in the penis, or the hole is small, or it is not in its place. 
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary, then he must perceive all of the spatula very finely according to this form:  
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put or through it a thin cloth of flint, and bind it and keep it so for three or four days and when he wishes to urinate, remove the clot, and let him urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps it does not come about, because the urine which comes forth does not leave it closed. 
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	The one whose wound is small, if it is medicated with the cloth of lead as we have said, then it will widen. 
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the penis in its place are pale, because none are born with the penis at the head of the shaft, so they cannot urinate until they raise their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come to the opening, and this is a bad disease. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies supine on his back, and they support the head of the penis and the scrotum as if it were a feather, so that the opening falls in the middle, as it should; and beware of bleeding which often comes from it, and if it happens, have someone who stanches blood stanch it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the blisters of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these blisters come in the penis, and it is a bad appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so it behooves you to pick them with one fine needle, and scrape and cleanse them all, then put cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment on top; then cure with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the boil is malignant, of bad color and pus, then you must bring fire cautery to it. 
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have grasped it, and if the [bone] is in its socket and part inside and part outside, then it is necessary that you remove the [bone] which is inside first; and when it is united, then you care for the outside. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Car when you treat it together, make sure the head of the stick is not pierced, and black rot and corruption come in its shaft and at the groin; so it must be cured all that is black and corrupt, then put a layer on the wound made from honey and flour which is made from peel of quince trees and myrtle, then treat it with other dressings until it is healed.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a bleeding occurs, administer the lunar cautery according to this form: 
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps with two things together: namely, bloodletting and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then you must put or lead from the penis a chain of wool, and urinate on the patient among; and when the skin is raw at the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or there is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you scrape it with the instrument's tip, until the bonds are untied, and the head of the penis is delivered on all sides; and if it is a painful thing to discuss this, it is necessary that you scrape it with the spatula some point at the head of the penis and the skin; then separate well between the two, and put the subtle linen cloth soaked in cold water, so that it does not dry.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like other wounds in terms of continuity; however, when we do this work of our will, and properly to children, it is necessary that we make the best possible work and the most light for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not perform circumcision on their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted the most greatest part of the masters and the healers who made circumcision around .i. dal, and as forces, and to one whole novacule; if it was the keurs for he has .ij. toiles, and by adventure if one chops this above and remains that below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it is convenient to cut, and is the pain double, and to the purification which is dou dal is not assured the tip of the member; and to the purification of the knuckle by adventure escapes the iron, and runs the work, and many times they are born as if they do not need purification and I have wanted.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the modification which is made as forces to all the linen of thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut justly as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, so that it is equal in all, but that the thread be well laid in the skin; and that the manner of the first work is such as you make the child think, if he understands, that you do not force him to bind the thread around the shaft only, and then make him rejoice in all manners that you can; then make him be between your hands straight, and retort the forces between your hands or under your feet that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the shaft and blow or heart, and bring it up until the head of the shaft is inside; then cleanse it well of the dirt that is gathered there, then bind the place with a double thread, then tie it below I with another thread; and hold as II does by the second link to the pouch and to the index finger, and cut between the II links, then raise the heart above gently and treat the head of the shaft; then leave him to let blood little by little, because that is the cure; and put powder on and on the powder I drape it with a half of a boiled egg tempered with rose water, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it until the next day, and cure it from other cures until it is cured.  
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces to the mundification is this: the two shoulders are held and are pointed, and the shoulders are also as large as the hands equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the mundification is when the pliers inside are at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your finger so that the lead makes an abscess; and cut equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then take tongs, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pierce for .iij. days, and what is below the rod is swollen, let it remain until the abscess has calmed, and lightly peel it; then cut as much as you can move, and guard the part of the rod, it will not harm it at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the place of things suddenly wound with powder, that we have said or treated about powders, and if one cuts too much with the pliers, and it goes upwards, it will not harm; cure therefore, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is from a stone in the bladder, or blood congealed, or bowel, or new flesh, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not relieved, and you see that the retention is due to a stone which is at the bottom or neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent on their knees; and that his feet be placed on his back, and extend his belly from the top towards his back, and restrain the patient's legs as much as he can; and thus the neck of the bladder is constrained to express the stone upwards, so that the urine is relieved; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer extraction with all the instrument which is called "syringe", from which this is the form: and be of fine silver, light tip, like the feather of a bird; and be the shaft one palm long and a half, and be fine at the top. 
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie it to the head of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and put it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and aubine of egg, and make the patient sit on the seat, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and tepid water; then gently put the syringe into the penis, until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis upwards towards the scrotum; then put the syringe forward until the bladder, and feel the patient come until the void thing, and this is not done according to this order for that because the conduit or where it goes is twisted; then extend the thread to all the wool head and head, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it, and do correct the urine; and restart the syringe as long as the bladder is emptied, and the patient is aligned. 
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scalds or blood comes in the bladder, or putrefaction is assembled there, and you see it distilling waters and medicines, so do it with all the instrument which is called "clepsydre," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed and if it has III openings: II on one side, and I on the other, as you see; and the lead should be such that the medicine stops well the rod without addition, so that if one can drain the moisture, and squeeze when necessary; and when you want to introduce your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the clyster in the moisture, and pull at the tube that is inside; so you will draw the moisture into the clyster, and then strongly push the tube back inside; so the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle clyster with which one clysters the bladder: this is it: 
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And is of silver or of copper, and is the head higher; and below to the chest where the ligaments fall; then take a sheep bladder and put in it the moisture that you see to clysterize the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts forming a good double cord, and heat the pouch of moisture on the fire; then put the tip of the clyster into the rod, then strain your hand over the bladder with all the moisture coming, until the patient feels that this moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make it the circle, and pierce it roundly around; then put the strong cord into these holes, then assemble the circle like one assembles the spindle, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, press your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder. 
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone engendered as rains, and all the signs, and in what stone one must work by size; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder often happens more to children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder seeming like water in its subtlety; and it appears hard, and pains the patient's penis, and he feels it many times, and then becomes soft; and with many of these jumps the foundations are formed; and it is light the healing of children until they have four years, and it is very painful in the elderly, and is as the middle for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to purify the patient by clyster, to draw out all the mucus which is in the intestines.  
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For he often encumbers to seek out the stone.  
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and loosen and move them downward so that the stone descends to the end of the bladder, and it comes out once from its place; then make him sit between your hands properly, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder is all declining down; then feel and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut above the stone. 
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall to the touch of all, then moisten your right index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your right middle finger, if the patient is an adult; and put it in its foundation, and search for the stone, and when you feel it with your right finger, aim at the bladder's neck; then press upwards on your right finger, and put it out in the direction where you want to cut. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the testicles upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the testicles in the part where the incision is made; then push the spatula cutting, of which this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And place between that which is between the buttocks and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left hip; and be right above the stone, and those two should be wide or foundation, and let the waist be traversed so that it is wide outside and inside narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, nor too large; perhaps the press on those who are or foundation, that she leaps out without work; and know that there are some stones which have angles, and margins: if it is cut a little; and if it is like one which is swollen, and rounded, whose issue is light.  
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	To those who have angles and margins, make the incision larger; and if it does not open, it is necessary that you extract it with tweezers that are like a file at the head, in order to extract the stone so that it does not escape; or you put underneath the subtle curved instrument at the head; and if you cannot engage it thus, then enlarge the small opening of the passage, and if it does not come out, strain it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stones, first put the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then push the larger one through, and the smaller ones afterward if there are many. 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then it must be treated, and make a larger wound. 
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For II things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes back through where the wounds cannot close; but nonetheless, you force to draw it out, or to break it with pliers, until you draw it in pieces; and when you have completed your work, then apply the wound of incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it up, and put on top the cloth moistened in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then bandage the patient on his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day. 
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, cleanse the area well with oil and water, then treat it with diaphicon ointment and basil ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if a boil comes in the wound and corrosions, and congealing of blood in the bladder, and by this retained urine, which is known in such manner that without jumping with the urine: therefore you must put it in the wound, and extract that blood, because if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and it will rot; then lift the wound with water and honey and silk, and help him in all the ways that you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the hours that you cure him, that you tie his two thighs together, and assemble the medicines on the place. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is located in the urethra, and tied in it, and the urine cannot issue; so the cure of these things, as I say, that you cut it many times, and there is an excuse for the cutting by this cure.  
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have proven this thus.  
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one piece of iron according to this form and be three corners hooked into one stick:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then put the forest in the shaft gently, until it reaches the stone; and turn the forest with your hand in the stone, point by point, until you can feel the stone on the other side; so urine will soon come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the shaft. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is immediately broken, and jump out with the urine, and heals the patient; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie one thread under the stone and the other above, then make the rod in place of the stone between the two threads, then extract it further, and untie the two threads, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed. 
de la piere des femmes	of the stones of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that a stone is engendered in women, and if it happens at any time, the cure is grievous, and it is forbidden for .iij. things: one is that by chance the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a knowing woman who will uncover herself to look at the stones, even when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well-knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more profound than the stone of the man, which is why it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and great fear there is. And if necessity demands this, it is necessary that you take a midwife well-knowing, and at pains find one, and if you do not find one, point do not desire; cast a mire subtle; and present her a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do what you command her of the inquiry of the stone; and regard well whether the woman is a virgin: therefore it is necessary to put her behind or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, constrain it below her behind, and recommend that she put her behind or on the patient, and seeks and presses her left hand on the bladder forming. 
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it is necessary that she move it from great to small from the entrance of the bladder until below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the buttock, where it appears to be moved, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her waist above or below the stone, and let the tail be first small; then put the loin into the waist, if you feel the stone so close to the wound as much as the stone can go out, and know that many ways of stones are: namely, small and large and rough and soft, long and rounded, and which have reins. 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the appearances to know the outcome. 
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the stone does not come out, put ground vitriol on it, and hold it for an hour until the stone is softened; then return to your work, as long as the stone is in place, and have the instruments that I told you in the extraction of stones in men so that they can help you in your work; and if the stone does not come out, and it is from the artery which is cut, put the powder on the spot and hold it with bandages and dressings, and do not start again those things, and leave the stone and do not extract it any more, lest the patient die; then cure the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the limbs are numb, then return to your work, as long as the stone remains firm.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aqueous ramice is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white syfac, which is the substance from the center of the testicles that contains the egg; and it is called “syfac,” and at times it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is i.e., another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white syfac that we have said; and those have this point not.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice is so weak that it comes to the testicles, and that matter is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the buttocks, and this moisture has many colors: either it is declining to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or aqueous white, and this happens more; and these are the signs to know this assembly, because if it is white as we have said, then the abscesses reopens,  like a loaf of bread, and does not open the buttocks, because it has moisture all around. 
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper cloth, then the abscesses are covered with part of the egg, and for this reason it is thought that it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the glans and the foreskin, then it is felt well; therefore when you see know the color of the moisture, then suspect to all the introducer quarrells, because the form is before. 
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this therefore which comes after the introducer, judge of this which is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his ability and the repletion of his body; then lie him on his back, on something a little high, and put many cloths under him; then sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart of the armpits; then take the spatula lightly, and cut the skin of the armpits among them long until below the elbow, and let the cut be straight dividing the skin of the armpits until the white fascia, and carefully scrape according to your ability; then pierce the fascia plain of water at a wide opening, and extract all the water, and then put your swabs, and extend the fascia upwards; and do not touch the heart of the armpits, but only the fascia; cut all or by pieces equally the bone from him subtly, that if you don't cut it well sagely, he will return the water; and if the weft jump in your work, then put it back in its place when you have completed the work of the fascia; then assemble the two leaves of the heart of the armpits at a seam, then cure him as other wounds, until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the ulcer corrupted by another malady, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, in doubting the flowing of blood; then cut the point to all the suspender, and extract the ulcer, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut the other part as you have done the first evenly, then wipe away the blood, and put in the wound linen half soaked in rose oil; and put outside another piece of linen soaked in wine and oil, and put on top of the two cushions, and put above doubled cloth, and tie it over the entire bandage that is according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two strips, and use them of wool charpie according to this semblance and be assembled by stitching in the waistline of the breeches, and one of the heads prickles above the foundation up to the back, and the other on the side of the armpit; and the other two chief over the two angles, and be all assembled the restraint in the buckle of the breeches; and once is medicine this branch of cautery in place of a steel knife, and it is that you prick the cautery cultellar subtle, and cut the skin of the scrotum, and be scalded as we have said, so that the white syfac which contains water is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syfac at once, and scorch it with this subtle hot cautery: 
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cope in all the manners that you can, as long as you scrape everything; and keep that the fire does not touch the eye; and know that this work is more safe; and move guarding of a decrease of blood, and moves that the works of size; and if nothing makes you contrary, or abscess cauterize or decrease of blood or other thing, so cure what makes you contrary, according to what is before said. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this work because of its horror, then administer a perforation as I have told you; and when you are certain by the signs that we have said that the watery root is there, make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below with all the spatula wide, and put the perforation to the long one of the body; and let the opening be wide so that all the water flows out; then put cotton on the spot and bind it, and leave for it to drain the remaining water, then cure it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to flow out at the mouth of the wound, then you should pour in a pen or instrument with which one treats the water from dropsy, of which the form is above; and widen the hole of the wound, and know that the water returns, and it is assembled after six months or until it heals, and when it is assembled as before, and so will pass the days of the patient.  
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this branch there is fear in many positions, so I seem to you it is best to leave it; and I will tell you the work and appearances of the abscess. 
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, and also to the joints; and this is for many reasons.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to know by superfluity sour and acute, which is spread to the joints, or by percussion; and it is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and finds no pain, and it is a serious abscess; and by adventure there are some abscesses grievous fearful and stony, and of fuze color, and at times comes from the outside of an artery, or from an inflammation of the vein. 
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is by the artery, then it is known by the arrangement of hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and it is not fitting that you touch it. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of the swelling of a vein is known by his disposition to the expression of the touch of the fingers, and can well make the size on this appearance, and on the other charrs; and it is that you cut the core of the veins, then the egg is in the top, and the trail fur of the white syfac, and deliver the suspender from all parts of the egg. 
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already cooked with these kinds of nees, then it behooves you to draw out the egg, and chop it; and if it is airs at the syfac, or in that which is within the vessels, then it behooves you to deliver all of that, and chop it roundly. 
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the cartilage is at the rear or front, it behooves you to cut it entirely, and remove the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the works are accomplished, then apply the wound to wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then cover it with other dressings until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a covering resembling the burgeon, with the softening of the boils, and the patient cries out when he walks; and the cure for this disease is as terrifying as the one before it, and nonetheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.  
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It behooves you to make the patient sit on a raised seat, then put the suspensory of the testicles down towards his hips, on all the vessels that are near the penis, and have the masters cover them, and stretch them forth; then cut with the sharp spatula wide through the middle between the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples; then put a needle where the thread is double, and tie it at the first place where the vein has come, and tie it straight to the other end; then cut them in the middle straightly, according to the length of the body, and pull out the corrupted moistures; then cure the wound as with others where one injures a bowe, so that no vessel leak that nourishes one of the testicles; for through these no evil comes, and if to all the vessels comes blood, it behooves you to drain the testicles in all the vessels; so that the toes do not lose their nourishment for the incision of the vessels, and dry up and cannot be aided. 
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the hip
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The happenings of this ailment are by the section that comes or where it's located, or the extension on the belly in the part of the flanks, for which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the corners; and this rupture is either of the syfac, or of the extension of it, and these II manners of much causes: whether by percussion, or jump, or fall, or lifting of heavy load, and similar things; and the signs when it's of the extension of the syfac, are that they come poc and poc, in long time, and doesn't come suddenly; and the abscesses are even until near the parfont, for which the syfac presses on the intestines. 
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the section of the pus, that it brings a sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear diverse, under the skin near, and this because of the issue of the intestine and the body to the outside of the pus.
