Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes these (abscesses) touch with the intestine, and are held in, and cause great pain to suffer to the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, because it is necessary to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the work is that you command the patient to bring the intestine to his hand inside the wound, if he can enter it; then be supported on his neck between your hands, and lift the hips; then raise the heart above, and cut all the skin of the groin from long; then put into the folds of the waist needles according to what you need to open the wound, and let it be such that the eyes may issue; then scrape the fascia that is below the skin of the groin, until the white fascia is uncovered on all sides; then put your index finger in that which follows the groin, in that which is between the white fascia which is under the skin of the belly, and between the second fascia, and depart that which is behind the belly, and between the second fascia; and then move with your right hand inside the heart of the groin, and keep the white fascia on top to your left hand, and raise the belly towards all the fascia towards the waist; and command the minister that he extend the belly upwards, and untie what is behind the ligament; and examine with your fingers if there is no intestine enclosed or white fascia hard, and if you find any of these things, put it into the belly below; then take a needle which has a thick thread made of X threads, and put it in the back part of the fascia, which is after the skin of the groin; after the waist, then cut the hairs that appear from the threads, until there are IIII threads; then assemble them one above the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the fascia, of which we have said that it is below the skin of the groin, with a strong thread of II parts; then enclose the hairs of the threads, and tie them together in the form of II parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter inside, except for pus which does not come; and put the thread straight according to the first long thread of II parts, and after these II threads leave the fascia which is below the heart of the groin the length of a finger; and after all the other according to the roundness that the belly carries; then cut in the part which is below the skin of the groin, as much as the sinew, and the bow, as we have said before; then bring moistened wool in oil, and put it into the wounds, and put on the thread that we have said. 
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at no time is the white groin that we have said cauterized after the incision, out of fear of a decrease in blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and let the thread hang until it dries through; and if it delays in drying, then be raised with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it dries; then cure the wound with another cure, until it is perfectly healed. 
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this practice, I never saw anyone who dared to cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made like the twig which is assembled with the branch, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after the cut above or lightly below; then cut in the middle, and cure the abscess of those who operate, as long as the vessels bleed; and cure it as we have said, until it is healthy. 
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	At no time comes a rupture in the angles, as we have said, and opens the eyes; and do not insert any of the intestines into the anus, and if there are any inserted, it is little, and repairs all hours; and anyway, if it remains too long in this point, it believes the wound or syphilis, until the intestine emerges; and this happens because of the extension of the syphilis which is in the angles, as we have said, because it is extended, then softened and swollen the eyes and opens; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and at no time is cured by iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies soundly on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the rupture inflated with a width according to the quantity of III does; and then extract the syphilis which is under the skin that the usual one, then take the root and put it on the place appearing of the syphilis; and press it at the full length of the belly, then stitch the II places appearing of the syphilis onto the head of the root, and stitch them both; then extract the head of the root, and do not cut the syphilis or extend the web or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the ramice of the intestines; then cure by the cure of wounds.  
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, then make him understand and care for the wound until it is healed. 
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The thigh is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles softens in certain men, because the contents within are softened, and it is visible; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and he cuts the skin which is softened over the natural skin; then join the two lips with a suture, and if you see it, first sew the superfluity of the softened skin with three or four sutures firmly; then cut between the sutures, and cure it like other wounds, until it is healed, and tie the thread.
dou chastrement	of the cauterization
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that chastisement is common in our law, and for this reason I would like that I speak not of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two manners: one of which is that the wise men know how to answer when they are asked, and know how to cure; and the other, because we often need chastisement from some beasts to help us, such as goats and sheep and cattle and other beasts. 
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I therefore say that cauterization is done in two ways: either by attraction or by incision. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, make the beast sit in hot water until the joints are softened and pliable; then take them in your hand, as long as they are put back and you no longer feel them. 
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the chastisement of tail: it behooves you to hold the beast and press its skin with your left hand, then tie the suspensory, and cut on each end at a point, when you will have well scraped them; and leave no prickle or subtle prickle that is on the vessels; and this manner of chastisement is better than that which is done by attraction, for that in attraction nothing remains perhaps from the testicles, so the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed. 
des hermofrodites	of the hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is according to II manners as men: one is if between the II sexes it opens as well as the figure of nature of a woman, or he has hair, and sometimes in short the urine. 
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and it is on the pubic bone as well as a shaft and two bones.  
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the cure of man and woman is that you cauterize all the joined parts, and cure them like other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine flows through the skin of the genitals, there is no cure. 
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a char attached to the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is the cure.  
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you take the superfluity of the tissue with your hand or tongs, and cut lightly; and do not go too deep, so that bleeding does not come, then cure it with another cure until it is healed; and in a different way that arises at the mouth of the marsh, and the temple, and perhaps jumps out, and is according to the semblance of a cow, and for this reason they call it the ancients "cow disease". 
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary that you cut it, as we have said the origin, and cure it until it is healed. 
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental by illness that it has come; or it is by a joint attached, or by a subtle or thick syfac, and is made in the middle, or in the ribs, or below, or wherever; and prevents conception, and pregnancy, and perhaps the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is by the gaze of the bailiff. 
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the stupefaction is approaching, so do at your two or at the side.  
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is with a subtle syfac, and it is near the two leaves, then hurry, and do this: put your two fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, spreading her legs; then extend the two leaves, until the subtle syfac is round, and is covered by the stupor; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and put it on the place, and let the woman lie at home each day, so that she cannot move. 
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the sty is hard and thick, then you must cut it with a spatula similar to a myrtle leaf. 
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stuffing is of flesh, then suspend it to the  incision and the edge; and apply medicines that stop blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, a mixture with an egg yolk; then administer a piece of broad plank so that the wound cannot close; and thus for length, and apply a tent of dry linen; then be cured by other cures until it is healed. 
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a new carbuncle comes in the flesh, it is to be covered according to this manner, unless it is an incured abscess. 
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that is festering in the marsh, one should not touch with fire. 
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without custom, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hardened; and we have said in the division the resemblances of them, and the signs, and I will say here those which resolve cure.  
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and boils, when they are made deep in the flesh, and do not appear to the touch, except for the cauterization by iron. 
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marsh, one can feel them, are those one can cure. 
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then hold the altar with tongs and cut it at its roots, then powder on medicines restraining blood, such as acaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet to the fire for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding comes, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and hawthorn and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and asafoetida, and apply a poultice on her back. 
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he endures it, it is good.  
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If this does not work, make an opening with the bellows on the back and breasts without hurting; then take linen and moisten it in juice of plantain or in elderberry juice with old wine, and apply the bellows to the place. 
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, care for its place with ointment until it is healed; and the one called "albathir" is red, and is similar to the harsh chief, so it should be covered as I have said in the previous; and then the care until it is healed.  
des apostemes de la marris	of the abscesses of the marshes
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many ways of abscess come in the marshes, such as chancre and puss-filled abscess and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and more other diseases that I have said in the division. 
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, it is necessary for me to say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marshes, which is not like abscesses that boil over; and if you want to know the work of iron, look at whether the abscess is thick at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it. 
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not haste thyself to pierce, but let him rest until the pain is appeased; and then make the patient sit on a seat, and have small seats where he leans, and supports his back and places his feet toward the parts beyond the leg; and let his thighs be spread out, and put his arms below his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then move him gently to the right side, and there administer the instrument with which one operates on the mouth of the abscess, so that what comes after is the form; and it is necessary when you see administering this instrument, that you first put the point in order to know the depth of the abscess, so that what enters inside the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the abscess with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt him; and let it put the cone of the instrument above, and hold the instrument.  
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and one makes it soft with the hand, then it is necessary to cover it with a cloth at the head, on the spatula of lead; and when the bowe is emptied, then it is necessary that you put in the wound wet tents in rose oil, or in dry green oil; and put the tent further from the wound to the edge of the margin, and put outside over the margin and on the linen sponge washed with water or mallow be boiled; then cure after II days of oinement before this, until it is healed; and no time lift the margin and the wound by clistere of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lilies and long arctitis are cooked; then return to the ointment. 
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is put back in its place, then you must be careful not to cauterize it with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division. 
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is first necessary for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing down, and desiring to smell the air: then she hastens the child to be born; therefore you know that this birth is according to the natural figure, and it is the head first, and the second comes with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly so that the child comes forth quickly; because when it descends on its head, the second comes with it, and the womb is cleansed of its superfluities by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.  
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes comes upon his feet, and comes forth from the body or the shoulder, and the hands, or where it comes upon his belly, or groin, and is turned by chance onto his neck, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary that the healer be wise and subtle in these things, and wary of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must aid them. 
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the fetus comes forth on its head by natural delivery, and the woman is laboring hard, and her strength is weak, then make her sit upon a saddle, or let the women hold her up; and anoint her behind with oil or fenugreek that is cooked, and then put the midwife between her thighs, the small spatula whose form is here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the secondine, and cut at its nail until the moisture that is inside it comes out; and hold the belly of the woman as long as the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to administer a clyster to the woman of fenugreek with sesame oil; then make her suck and sneeze from condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: thus now will the child come.  
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands are coming out, it is necessary that you gently push them in and out; and if they cannot enter, put the woman on the seat, and lift her feet up; then tilt the seat onto the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall during the tipping; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut the hands at the neck which is placed before, and extract the child, and reset evenly. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the child on his feet 
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes upon its feet, it is necessary to push them up; and then turn them back and forth, until they are even; then grip its feet and extend them back and forth. 
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Until he jumps to his hips, if you command him to take it, and make him sneeze by condition; if it works, may God will. 
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not healed as we have said, then turn it back and forth, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come forth as we have, say take a muslin cloth of linen, and oil of sesame, and melted wax, and grind all in the mortar; and put upon the nature of the woman within and without this ointment, then make her sit in a warm bath until under the ribs; and when she is softened beneath, make her a coliere of myrrh, and put it beneath, and let her remain an hour; then make her sit upon the stool, then make her sneeze and restrain her mouth and nose, and gently take hold of her belly, because the child will now jump.  
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, he places his hands fist and fist; then it is laid on its neck, and the feet hang down, and lying on the bed; and bends his hands fist and fist, and then takes his hands on his belly, and removes the cushions below, until she is prepared downwards; and if the child does not jump, he takes his feet and moves them forcefully, then moves the belly upwards, then puts his hands; and so the child fist and fist; and commands to the woman that she be in charge as long as the child jumps.  
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the delivery of the child which comes out with a broad hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It behooves to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, then make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, then have her lie on the bed, and spread out her legs; then administer the poultice that I have recounted; and if she does not give birth, then have her sit on the stool, then try to bring back the hand; and let the child be according to the natural figure, and have her sneeze, and command her to suckle as long as the infant needs. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child on his neck, and has spread his hands, and his face turned towards the back of his mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is fitting that the patient should hold his hand, then turn it back and forth, and the other gently; and when it is equal, he places it upon the nature muscle of height and oil, as we have said, then commands her to move back and forth; and when you have done this, sit her on the seat, and command her to strain; and she will sneeze.  
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of this same manner to all of the spine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to be in this manner to the whole back, so cut the back at your finger, until the moisture is emptied; and if the child leans upon his face and upon his neck, so cut out of the bud, that she not be held, and let the child die; then put the child inside, as long as you have put him as it is right, and command to the woman that she preens no time: then it will lightly straddle. 
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and they do not live, if it is possible to name them; I know that they should be multiplied, and they are severed by the soul which divides them, who is bound to the head; and sometimes they go out as naturally as all others, as we have said.  
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are pricking painfully, the treatment as we have said, and let the healer be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what it does; and do thus as he will save them. 
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	At no time are they formed in the marsh I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of his glorious sage, and it is necessary that the bail knows all these, because by chance similar things happen; so do as it is necessary. 
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the dead child or belly, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands; it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or she has fear of death; it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back, and her shoulders be inclined down, and her legs raised; and the minister the sheet of II parts, or she is tied to the bed so that she is not treated in the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the belly with moist oils with muslin of althea and fenugrec and flaxseed, then anoint the hands with these oils and these muscillages; then put them into the belly gently, then desire the place where she puts the pins to be convenient to those, and take ward if the child is appearing that it descends on his head; if they put the pins in her eyes or in her neck or in her mouth or in her palate or under the beard or in the throat or near the ribs, and if the descent is on feet, then they put it or prick and as sides; and it is necessary that he holds the pin in his right hand, and puts the curvature between his two of the left hand, and puts them to all his hand gently, and puts the pin in any of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the pin: 
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then place against the other bone where you need it, so that the extractions are equal; and then make them equal in moving from one side to the other, so that it may be moved, and let the bones have teeth so that they may hold, as this is the form. 
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if part of it remains, he anoints the joint with some of his oil and puts it in that part, and draws the other part; and if none remain, he places this ointment or higher and does so until it all comes out entirely. 
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be brought back by tightening, then you should wrap it on the drape, until it is whole; then cut at the joint of the foot or to the knife, and so it is necessary that you do in the other hand, and as with II feet. 
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's hip is large and it is strained at the exit, or it has a sharp chief assembled, then you must put the pointed spatula between your two, and make the chief and extract the sharp; or you can do it with the instrument which is called "almidach," because its form comes with the instruments or chapter which is after this one; and in the same way do if the child has a great chief naturally; and then pull the bones apart with the pliers, and if the hip jumps out and it is strained with force, so be broken, until the moistors which is or worse exit; and if it cannot issue, then cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then you must pierce it as long as the moistors run.  
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the application to the mouth of the cavity is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is abroad in the belly or breast, then you must draw it out to the cloth wrapped around the hand; and make the belly or breast, as long as the moisture that is there corrects; and if the other member are taken away, and the head remains, then put the bail your hand into the midst of the mouth; and drag it up to the mouth of the fissure; then put the hook or pin in, and drag further; and if the mouth of the fissure is constricted because of a hot abscess that has come, then it does not need to be labored; rather, moist and fatty things must be administered; and administer plasters, and seeds in soft and moist water.  
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, then administer what we have said in a living child; and if one has no power, then treat it by parts, and leave nothing of the backbone. 
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if they administer to them what we have said in abscesses that come in the marshes; and if bleeding occurs, it is put into sharp restraining, and they are given other treatments. 
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly one child had been stillborn, then conceived another upon that one, and miscarried the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time she had an abscess in the wound, and it swelled so much that it opened and began to drain greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I pondered for a long time, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I placed a strong adhesive plaster upon it, and after some days one bone came out, and after some more days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly, because this one whose belly has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I cauterized the wound, and in manipulating the bones, until the woman was in a better condition; and the woman stayed long like this, and it grew back a little of bone from its place; and I have not recorded this chapter further than because when the master finds an unusual thing, that he knows how to put aid. 
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the bone back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here after comes the form of the forceps, how it is made in books; and at two turns at two joints of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns shall be more subtle of the restrictor, and be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the pipe should be of a large width, and the edge of the trees it must, and long one palm and a half; and between the two limbs should be two adjustments of this same pipe, which are fastened in one and the other, of half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are put into the mouth of the muzzle to open when one turns the two horns. 
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, of its semblance more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the semblance of pliers; and has II chiés II adjustments, as you see, one palm long, and II wide; and when you see opening the mouth with all the instrument, so make the woman sit on the bed, her feet hanging down and legs open, then put the II adjustments adjusted together in the mouth, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then work your hand on all the instrument, as you have done with pliers equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the vagina, until the girl does what she wants. 
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all mounted and are multiplied their likenesses; and when the eyes have appeared them, so much more hasty is the work, and higher to men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument that you have not appeared it, because their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained during childbirth, it is necessary that you command the woman to retain her breath, and then make her sneeze with condiment, and restrain her hands at her mouth and nose; and if she jumps through this, well is it. 
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If this is not done, then take I a pot, and make I it pierced or covered, and I put therein herbs that may open the mouth of the marsh, such as calament, rue, anise, chamomile, cassialigne and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, be cooked or boiled in water on the fire; then place one end or opening of the pot in the mouth of the marsh, and the other end in the mouth of the marsh, and keep it there until vapors come from within the marsh; then I make it sneeze, as we have said.  
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second part jumps hastily.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this cure, and there is no strength, then command the midwife that she moisten her left hand in oil of sesame or in liniment of aloe, and then put it into the nature, and seek the second time; and when she has found it, she grasps it and extends it back and forth straightly, so that the marrow does not fall out during the extraction; but it should be moved lightly to right and left, and then pulled; so it will come and detach itself.  
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the marsh is tight, we have said the cure of sneezing, and fumigation of herbs; and if it is not from all that we have said, so guard that you do not use the milk; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the marsh, that you tie it to the hip of the woman, then enema with ointment tetrafarmacon; if it will open and return, and come forth; but nonetheless, when it opens, there comes bad odor to the stomach and head, and pales the sick person. 
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore it is necessary fumigations suitable for that: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for the retention of flowers and the second thing is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And is to see the appearance of a dog, and one puts the head subtle in the nature, and the shoulders wide above the fire; and let the fumigation be on the coals, and the tar as long as it is wasted, and begin another.  
de percier lou fondement	to consider its foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but it is stopped with a subtle syfac: so it behooves the midwife to pierce that syfac at its due, and do not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and guard the bandage so that it does not touch; then put a soft linen cloth in wine and oil, then the cure of ointment until it is healed.  
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it does not close up again, then put on a poultice of flax, and leave it for several days, and remove it when the child wants to go into the chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stoppage comes from a swelling of a wound or abscess; so it is necessary to cover that swelling: if it is cured, as we have said of the cautery of pitch.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the foundation are nodules, and larger ones that come from near the foundation outside, or in the space of the two parts, if there is a fistula or more; and when that nodule is old, it works, and still moist moisture awakes white or subtle bowe, and sometimes these fistulas disappear; and they are known by those who have them for excretion or venting when the patient makes an excretion, and perhaps in jumping some.  
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if the fistulas that pierce to the bladder, and to the middle of the penis; and reach to the joint of the groin, and to the root of the scrotum.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula passing to the foundation, and not passing: and it is that you put your thumb or foundation, and put a fine needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twisting.   
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is torsion, then it puts in a tent of fine silk or horse hair, until you feel the tent or hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and it does not come out through purgation or flatulence or pus, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; so hasten to cure. 
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced up to the bladder or to the urethra, if it leaks urine and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the joint of the hip, then the tendon comes up to the place; if there is no torsion and the invention of pain around, then there is an abscess, and there is no worth of medicine or healing by ointment; and in these piercing fistulas there is no cure other than labor, and vanity of foolish wonders who intervene. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one who is neither very young nor very old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lift his legs up to his hips, and let his hips be inclined to his belly; then put a tent of linen, or of fleece if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent comes.  
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it near the base, then you must put your index finger there, and feel if the finger touches it; and be uncovered where you feel between your finger the sinew or the flesh, then you know that it is pierced; if you do not work upon it, one cannot heal it. 
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One says however that one can well heal none, but this happens rarely; and the help that one makes, if one heats the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before; and thrusts it all hot into the fistula, until it comes near the foundation; and do this two or three times, as long as you know that these charred hairs are burned, which are like a feather of an eye; and then cure with wet bandages in butter, as long as those hairs exit, then cure with ointment healing flesh and joining. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If so it is healthy, well. 
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this is the case, it cannot be healed in any other way; and if it sticks between, and does not pierce to the depth which is the foundation, and between your two depths and the tent a thick covering of flesh or of fat, and you see the fistula at this covering following the heart; so cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push forward the tent, and then apply the cautery after, as long as it comes to the head of the tent; and will be delivered the tent, and fall away; then remove those faults of flesh that seem like a feather of an owl, and none remain. 
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood vein goes wrong, and it comes between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or with sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Because the fire cauteries assemble II good things: that is to know, the burning of these joined bones and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; then the cure of damp wounds in butter or in crushed herbs, as long as the skin remains soft, and if the joins are burned in the softness; then cure the wound of solid suppurations by enclosing hard flesh, and they are dry medicines. 
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes just to the root of the foundation, and is removed from the body, then you put your finger or foundation there, and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between there is the cloth or the syfac or chariots, where it is near to piercing, if there are no other means than by way of faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three ways: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put tents and cure it as first; and do not go too much in depth, that you do not cut the tenement that holds the foundation, and the egestions come by the voluntary will; then cure, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the mund after it is cut from its foundation, or by tent or by another pointed instrument; then defuse the char fautree which is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part outside the foundation: it will be a lighter thing for the patient. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner: and when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is or on the side of the foundation near the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the top according to this form: 
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he puts one thread wrong in two, and puts the tent to all the thread in the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is piercing in the margin of the foundation within, then extract the thread of that which is pierced, just as you place your hand or foundation; and treat the head of the thread, and assemble the two heads together, and restrain one to the other, and let it rest for a day or two; and restrain it no time, until the threads cope those carts that are between two, and stick together; then cure the wound until it is soldered and healed.  
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not become to make for the lacing cover if too deeply embedded, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spinal spatula used to make a fistula is very hard on one side and trenchant; and on the other side no, because for that reason one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here. 
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhages are according to II manners: or they are within the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in short, a little blood, and there are one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are outside have less moisture, and still a little of clear water or a little of blood, and have the color of the body; and the cure of those who have them inside the foundation, is that you command the patient to stretch himself to go into chambers, as long as the foundations come out, and appear the filaments; if haste, and can hold it with tweezers, or you hold it with your finger, then cut it at its roots; and if the pincers cannot hold it because of its moisture, take it with the sheet, or with cotton, or a piece of felt; and remove it to your fingers, then cut it, and powder above some hot powders that are in its place of cautery; or you cauterize it as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure the other cures until it is healed; and if the foundations cannot come out, you give the patient a purgative and harsh enema to wash what is in the foundation, so that it can come out openly; when the patient stretches, and if the filaments are outside the foundation, the cure is light; and it is that you take them with your finger or tweezers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until it is healed, and that he fears the incision by iron. 
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you administer the suture in this manner: take one thread and put it into a needle, and then draw the thread upwards and make the needle pierce on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and so be wide; and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, and leave one to correct the superfluity of blood; then place on top of the foundation a soft cloth in rose oil or in cerate, and place on top, and command the patient to rest; and then let it rest until they are dry, and when they are dry, cure them with ointment and other cures, as long as it is healed.  
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the drying of the veins or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a drying up of veins in the intestines, and by constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you reset to the point of a spatula or your fingernail the bark above, which does not let it moisten; then treat it until it is closed as it should; and if it cannot close, restart the scraping stronger than before, until it heals well, and is barked; then treat it until it is healed. 
dou fremit	when it trembles
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are a small appearance, false before the body, and go much into it; and sometimes it is found cold, and feels one as though dead from trembling, and comes throughout the body, and more to the hands than elsewhere. 
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a stick of an goose feather, or a powerful vulture feather, and put that stick on the wound, until the purple circles reach all around the wound; then turn your hand over the entire stick until you cover all around the wound, and place it in depth, and scrape the wound from its roots. 
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this of a dog of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and long above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce it, for must keep to the two, and move pressed And if you see, so cauterize the edge, as it is before or chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No time made one enema of silver or lead, or iron melted or woven; and no time is made of these instruments small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore those who are administered in the cure of the children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the enema, small and large, so it is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this manner.
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And there is an incision where the belly is bound, as you see, and the head is pierced inside; and on one side it has two holes, and on the other one; and the belly is where one puts the medicines of a beast's bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and between each hole there is one space, then put in these holes a strong thread of twisted thread X or whatever around, and assemble the belly as it is a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie the strap in front with a strong thread, then give a clyster; and this is the form of the circle: 
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg yolk or something similar, then insert it gently; then squeeze the minister's hands together until it is all visible, then withdraw the clyster, and lift the patient’s legs to the side, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it flow as much as it can; and if he sleeps a whole night after, it will be more of a help. 
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you enema him in the sickness of belly falling, and the medicine hastens to spread, so begin again until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the base, or abscess, then use the clyster as subtle as for a child; and that is the shape of the subtle clyster on which the skin is restrained: 
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the cure of wounds; or we will tell you the cures of hands and medicine, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the strike of a stone, and the size of a sword and knife, or lance or staff or dart, or similar things; or that are done according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the back, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with wounds of the head simple, because remembrance will come in its chapter.
