Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, if you are careful it is of gallstone or similar things, and the skin is immediately torn and the wound is large, and you doubt greatly an abscess hot: so make it bleed immediately from the cephalic same as if it comes a little blood from the wound, and let the bleeding be contrary to the part numbed; and avoid the patient's repletion of wine and thick meats. 
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, let his meat be diminished, and he shall not drink wine, nor shall he eat meat; and put on the wound, if an abscess comes there, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in styptic wine; and if there is no abscess hot, put on the wound, if it is fresh to all its blood, and it has not been moved by the air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if it has moved, put on some ointment until he is healed. 
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a cut from a sword and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by tenting, then assemble them by stitching, as I will say for wounds of the belly, of the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is open to the bone, and hangs, and holds only by a thread, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as beef and cooked barley, as well as poultry, and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a rotting skin, and it reaches the bone, so cut away all the rot, and throw out its filth, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicines, then cauterize the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it. 
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and that you put into this powder which binds as soon as the arsenic has healed it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood II parts; quicklime III parts, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and strain it well, until it dries well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it untied, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time is this made with only quicklime, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but that the heat has cauterized the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the one who cuts has made a wound, even in being so, then don't put on this powder; but put some dressings digested, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, as long as it swells. Then cure with other cures until it is healed. 
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers; and I will tell you here afterwards about the fractures of the head. 
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes from the neck and it is simple, if it has no difference between this and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other thing to leave the cure, and do not put anything restraining, because it harms the nerve and makes them retreat; and do not put on the wound anything cold, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of this is with the brain, which is the highest member; but be the medicine warm, such as calx washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cucum root also washed in sweet water, and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist ointments. 
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it and bind it with bandages, then tend to it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is hollowed out and full of bowe, pierce or lower there; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding comes, then cauterize it, and close it up, and cauterize as necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the vein, and the conduit is kept, so that the flesh goes, sew the heart above the chain of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural form; and then restrain it well, and leave it some days, then cure with ointments as long as it is healthy; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then set it; and if there are pieces of bone, take them out all that you can, and those that you cannot have, then let them be until the wound rots and is cleaned up; and if the wound is fresh, then put powder on top of the powder that I said. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if it has bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the lance or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a lance or sword, and the wound is deep, see that from the wound no wind is escaping as the patient breathes; know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh in all its blood, do not put any powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it tight to keep the blood from flowing out, and returning to the heart, and saving the patient; but put attractive ointment on it, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck up the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; so that no spasms, nor bad tremors of the heart, nor any pain in the chest come; and when you see good signs, then know that the wound is saved. 
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure therefore of tents and other dressings, as long as it is healing; and if it cannot heal, and operate, then know that there is a fistula; so treat it as one should.  
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or worse, on the back, then treat it as those in front; if it is large, sew it; and if it is small, use powder; and if it is embedded in bone, and has broken pieces, then clean the wound, and remove the fragments if they are loose; and if they are not loose, let the wound rot so that it will lighten the extractions; and for other wounds on other limbs, follow the judgments as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	about the displacement of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is great and medium and small; from the great wound sometimes the intestine or the nerves of the intestines come out, because of which the introduction of others; and the suture is more difficult, and sometimes it is worse the small wound than the large, because one puts back the intestines more easily, if one does not put them back hot in cold; because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, so they go back in more easily, and because of this, the medium wound is worse, because one must reset the intestine to its place like the others II And know that the rupture of the belly is according IIII ways: the II common sutures happen in the suture of the belly, and the suture of the other wounds of the body and II other sutures proper are common to the other wounds; and nevertheless they are more appropriate with the suture of the belly, and I will say one each and declare. 
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the entrails is outside, and it is a good thing to close it, this is done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is inflamed due to the cold. 
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in hot water only, or you boil in hot water thyme and cypress and spice, and apply the interior as long as the inflammation is removed; and sometimes do this restrainingly, and let it be moved that only to deflate. 
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or ale and make sure that they are cooked well, for by this is aligned the entrance to a little thing; and if it cannot enter, then make a hole in the wound with the instrument of which one cuts hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to be more than the tail, which no one should cut without great need; and this is the instrument to split: so cut inside in the curve and outside not, and see here the form. 
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines are pushed out, put it back in place according to its natural form if you have the power, because this heals. 
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower part of the belly, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, then put the head and buttocks higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, then put your attention to that the sunken part be higher than the other; and thus it is necessary to administer what I say in large and medium wounds.  
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, place what has appeared to you, then put in your hands the minister who holds all the rupture with his hand, and assemble the lips; and this is the common way of stitching, and it is that you prick an awl or more, according to the quantity of the breadth of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound I a distance, and there insert an awl where there is the good strong thread; and pierce the II chiez dou cuir with the II chiez dou siphac, which is under the skin inside, as long as you make it pierce from that part, and assemble the II chief dou siphac the IIII together; then strain a double thread around the awl of II parts, then assemble the II chiez de la plaie avenanment, and then leave I a distance, and there insert another awl; then tie the end of the thread as you did the first awl, and do not cease to do so according to what you need of needles, until the whole wound is constrained; and let the needles be medium, between subtle and thick, because the subtle needles cut all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot enter well: therefore it is necessary that they be medium; and it is not necessary to put the needles too far from the flesh and the skin, lest they cut and open the wound before the suture; and then cut the ends of the needles, so that they do not prick the patient when he sleeps, and put bandages or pieces of cloth at the ends of the needles for them to hold, and leave them until the wound is sewn together; and this manner of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds, because there one needle suffices or II the second suture is common, and it is that you assemble the II chiez dou cuir and the II chiez dou syfac together with an awl where there is the good medium thread; and when you have pierced these points all IIII together, you will move the awl to the part where you began, in the manner on which one sews the cloths; and put a distance between each stitch the thickness of a little finger; this suture was known by men, and I sewed a wound that a man had on his belly, who was wounded by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and the intestines were well II palms wide, and the wound was in the middle of the belly. 
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been out for XXIV hours, and the wound was closed until XV days, and I treated it, and he was healed. 
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the people had judged him to be dying, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in that place where one did not find any, nor any medicines; and I put on top of the wound cotton old II times a day, and I washed it with water and honey until he was healed.  
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of sewing: take the needle, and put it from the outside part to the inside; when it has pierced the heart straight in straight, let the tip through the skin or sewn where you have put the needle, and make it pierce from the other side from the inside part to the outside; and the understanding of this stitching is that you sew as the furrier makes the furs, and that you leave one time the skin on one side, and take it back on the other, until the sewing is completely finished.  
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of stitching, that the Galicians say properly, is like any font, which assembles the two parts together naturally, and applies one chief dou syfac to the other chief, in such a manner: stitch an awl or chief dou mirach near, and make it pierce only that place, and leave the two chiés dou syfac; then turn the awl, and make it pierce from the outer part to the inner part, at the two chiés dou syfac; then make it pierce both the outer and inner parts, at two other chiés dou mirach that are on the other side; and this is the most common manner of stitching. 
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galians says this word, and no one testifies it, one must sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each; and one must push one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew corrals; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the stitching is more grievous than the others of the belly. 
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is like that of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as long as the arrow has moved it, put back the intestines and the gut; then put powder on top, encasing the flesh, and if the arrow has moved it, put ointment on top that is present, until the wound bows; and stitch the edge, and be sure of the sinus, and the mirach; then cure the wound as with others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, put on, as soon as it begins to bow, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	Because you do not need other medicine in many situations where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not make communication with the principal members, then it is necessary that you moisten the linen lightly in oil of tempered heat, or in rose oil, and put it around the angles, and under the armpits; and if it feels pain or rot in the bowels, and many times happens, so the black wine enemas you, and likewise if the rot comes up to the intestine; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, then it is easier to heal than the small.  
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called «jeun» cannot heal when it is damaged, and this is because of the planting of the veins that are in it, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the closeness of its nature to the nerves.  
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the worm jumps from the wound, put it back as far as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned to black, then you must tie the place that is black, so that bleeding does not come from there, because there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligature, and put the two ends hanging from under the wound until outside to align the extraction when the worm falls, and the wound closes. 
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, one may be able to restore it in some men, because I have seen that a man was wounded in the belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and through this came the excretion and wind; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to treat until he was healed, and his bowels were joined. 
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him soldering, I feared that the patient was ill in his belly; and he had no pain, but remained in better dispositions, and eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in such a manner: take strips with large ends, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the strip has covered the mouth, put it on the two lips, so that it strains its mouth upwards; and then cut the end, and this stays so that it cannot untie itself, then put another strip afterwards in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely closed; and sew the wound.  
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	This chief if it is inflamed in the intestine, and there comes no nuisance to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the head of this thread of intestine that it be well cleaned, and then tie to the head of this thread the thread of linen fine twisted, then put the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it in the rupture; and this manner of sewing of bowels is nothing but according to the way of hope and expectation; and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is nothing else nor health, except for subtlety. 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called "fistula," and even when it is healed and re-closed.  
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the truth a knotted fault rough and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also feathered like the feather of an eye; and sometimes in clear bowe, and other times thick; sometimes pointed, and other times enough; and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is only by one of the IX causes: which is to know, by the little blood or body; or for its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the lips, that does not let flesh be born; or there is too much bowe; or the matter is rotten, and the material is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because corruption is a manner of pestilence; or because the property in the region is late digestion, and late healing, and inflamed by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Therefore it is necessary that I make you know the cure for fistula which is done by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the liver, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and so forth that it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar parts. 
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of bad healing, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place that I have said, and you have faith in the cure, and you want to know it, so take a tent of iron or of copper, if the fistula is straight, so the one; and if the fistula is crooked, so the encircle with a subtle tent of lead, because the lead bends well around the tortuosity; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot well surround it with tents, so irrigate it through one of the holes, because the moisture goes from one hole to another, and cleanses it; then the cover wisely in your power, that you know if there are bones or nerves, and is covered by force, and ask the patient well about the pain that he feels when pressing with your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you will truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from the joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, so cut according to what I have told you, and remove the foreign bodies and corrupted flesh that are inside; and then cure until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep straight place, so it is necessary that you cut as deeply as you can, then put moist tents in a medicine against ague, and put them up to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity which is at the bottom; and then put ointments healing good flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by these means, so cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, so cut it. 
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerves do not strike or principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then cure the king as long as the corruption is entirely removed, then care for things in order that it may be healthy; and if it is not healthy, and returns bent as before, know that you are not well gone to the font; uncover and seek as long as you are at the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healthy, it is good. 
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this does not occur, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot arrive there; if there is nothing else than to leave it to nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can extract it with pliers, if you extract it with an instrument suitable for this, and if there are many bones, then extract them all, do not leave even one; and if the moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cut both the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones. 
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, put on the wound something preventing rot, and leave until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then they will more easily separate the bones; and if it is a large bone, such as of leg or thigh, then keep only the corruption as long as the blackness is entirely removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part corrupted, and comes to the flesh of the bone; then it is necessary to be careful and cover everything until the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example from it and help in your work. 
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around XXX years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so much that the materials came to the leg and became inflamed with a large abscess, and there was no external cause to open; but the healers through their folly opened it so much that the abscess opened, and they drained a lot of material, and it became a fistula, and there came many openings that all oozed pus and moisture from the body; and many healers treated him for around II years, and there was no sage in the art of hands, until I was called to him, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what flowed through the openings to a great extent; and the young man's skin became red, and he had a yellowish color. 
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I put a tent in one of these openings, and then I searched all the openings, and found that one came against the other from all parts of the leg. 
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I therefore held it back and dug into one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, and I found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came up to the inner bone; I saw what appeared to me from the rotten bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except that which I had removed; and began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, and could not close it; and then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I saw it, and then I removed it, and I was about to close the place; but I could not, because when I dug around an inch of the bone, and it was broken all over, then I restored it with medicines; and it became healthy and closed quickly, and did not need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had for him. 
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For because of blood evacuation, often but he was healed entirely, and there was born in the place of the bone a hard cartilage, and was of good disposition and had no harm nor contrary at all in any way, neither to go nor to come. 
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, it is necessary to be treated in this manner: take a linen cloth, and bind it to the head of the bone which opens, and command someone that he stretch it upwards; and put another linen cloth thicker than the first linen, and tie it above the flesh which is below the bone, and extend the head, so that you draw the corrupted flesh downwards, and uncover the flesh in the place where you want to be, that the bone does not pierce the flesh; and put a piece of wood or a plank under the bone to move the corrupted flesh; and it is necessary to be as one can see and feel the corruption, and be again another time. 
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted, and it does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all of the flesh; then put tinder underneath, and then bring the fire from one side to the other, the corruption, and let the fire be long along the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and bring the bone or where it contains from the other part; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is nothing else to do but to cut; and if the corruption is in the finger of the hand, or in the finger of the foot, then that thing is very strong, but nonetheless, you must inquire about this corrosion, how it opens for you; and purify it in all the ways that you can, but that the vein or nerve do not make you go against it; and know that the instruments and threads for cutting these bones are many, according to the setting of the bones and the appearance of them, and their thickness and their thinness, and their size and their smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason, it is necessary to equip each kind of work with its instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of diseases; so consider the instrument that you need according to what it befits. 
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder can be injured either from within or from without; and when you have treated the corruption with medicines, and they do not benefit, then it is necessary to cover that limb up to the place where the corruption comes from, so that the patient escapes by this from death, or from the malice, which is greater, of the failure of the limb; and the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it seems as though it were burned by fire, and then after the blackness, follows the corruption of limb to limb, and takes over the whole body; therefore hasten to cover it, and if it is from the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as a sea scorpion and viper and similar ones, if the corruption is at the head of the thigh, then cover it, and do not give it any space to come until the hand. 
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, cut at the joint so that the corrosion does not come to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no other treatment except for the amount of its virtue; and thus do when the corrosion comes or foot: if it comes in the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, cut the entire foot; and if it rises up the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means than to leave the patient to death; and the manner of cutting or cauterizing the limb is that you bind it above and below, and extend one minister on the lower ligament, and others ministers the other ligament up, and you sever the flesh which is between the two ligaments at a spatule wide, so that the bone is uncovered; then cut or cauterize, and put on each side the drape of linen, so that the cautery does not touch the healthy part, and comes to the patient another lesion and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you work, cauterize the place immediately, or put some restraining powders on it; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the limb wounded with a suitable bandage, and cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: he had a blackness that seemed burned by fire, and that corrosion first came in his heel, until it encompassed the whole foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hurried to cover his foot, and was healed; and long afterward the corrosion returned in his hand, and he came to me, and I put on him things that are effective after the purification of the body, and could not stop the corrosion; and he told me to cut off his hand, and I refused, because I had hope of treating the matter; and also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the strength of the man was weak; and he despaired altogether, and returned to his land, and hurried to cover his hand, and was healed; and I have recounted this story only for this reason, so that one might do otherwise if they need it. 
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes in a fleshy place and stays so long that it makes a great gathering of pus; and then it bursts and drains, and the pus leaves its bed, as if it were vessels; and the skin which is above is as subtle as fine linen cloth, and does not go until to the bone or to the nerve, and such sickness is called “sain” and is not called “fistula”; but if it is so long that it comes until the bone, then it is called “fistula”; and the skin so is that you cut that skin all around, and even when it is subtle as fine linen cloth, and does not heal because of its corruption. 
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have faith that the skin is hardening, and the corruption is not in its full form, and the skin is thick with flesh, so treat it with a clyster like this: look if the breast is large, and the bow which is in it is of foul odor, then clysterize with Egyptian medicine which is made thus: take ash, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put them to cook in a vessel over fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey; and then take of this according to your need, and make it in water and honey, and clysterize the breast, and restrain the opening; and let the medicine remain inside for II hours, then remove it by pressing; do this many times, until the breast is cleansed, and the odor is removed; and sometimes clysterize with water of ashes, when this medicine is not present, and that you take ashes of vine wood, and pour water over them, then strain it, and clysterize, until you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot endure either the Egyptian medicine or the water of ashes, then clysterize with water and honey or have a little pounded litharge; or you clysterize with honey and sweetened wine, that the honey may have the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the flesh airy; and when you have done this, and you are certain that the breast is well cleansed, then clysterize with what causes flesh to grow in it, and that is that you take diaphanous plaster, and make it with rose oil and wine; or you clysterize with some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken the properties or treated of the ointments; and if the opening of the breast is small, and the tube of the clyster cannot enter, then enlarge it with an iron a little, and put inside a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basil oil, until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, then sew and leave only that place where the clyster can enter, and if the opening which emits odor is above, then apply the cup or lower the level where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bow is in place, one does not let anything impede its healing; and if you cannot cover the breast below as you want, arrange it in such a way that the bow goes to the lowest point where it is, for when the bow is in place, one does not let anything impede its healing and if you cannot cover the breast below as you want, arrange it in such a way: that the bow goes gently downwards, and do not leave anything of the bow; and take medicines consolidating to put on the sore, and stay on the linen cloth that covers the whole sore; then cut as much force into the opening of the breast as possible, larger than before; then apply ointment softly on the other cloth according to the quantity of the opening, and put it on the sore of the breast to align the bow, and do not remove the large cloth outwards except after many days once; and the one who is on the opening of the breast, often removed to remove the bow, and knows what flows from the bow, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digestible, or indigestible; and take note if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in this manner and you see the nature that jumps on the sore of the breast, then know that the breasts are already healing, and approaching health; and then untie it in the morning, or the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast lies bowed indigested after many days, know that the breast does not heal well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons cut after long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches. 
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose flesh heals slowly in their wounds, and some who heal quickly; and if a wound from the chest is bad after many days, know that the breast does not close well; and if the breast is slow to close and is enlarged, then apply drying medicines, moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diaphinit ointment, because there is much vitriol in it, and this is the last medicine. Take diaphinit ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the residue of old wine equal in substance; then confit it and use it; and the same thing made better honeyed, when diaphinit ointment is not present, or take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind it, and powder it on the honey when it is over the fire; and then glue it to the breast, and put some long licorice root and roots of celestial lily, which is also like flour from quince and wormwood; and use either simples or composites: grind them, and make them into powder, and put them on the honey that I said, and use it; and if the cure is lengthened, and is not cured by this cure, then know that the corruption is deep, and makes an impression in the bone, or in the hard limbs, or in the members; so cure the fistula, as we have said before. 
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the angle
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the hand, or of the foot, or perhaps in other places; and when it is neglected, and one does not take care of it, then the abscess grows, and runs and breaks down so much that it runs to the root of the nail, and perhaps all of it; and comes the running to the bone, as long as there comes a putrid pain, and is the limb of the foot wide, and is the color pale. 
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cut to it. make all the superfluity that is remaining from the joint, then cauterize the wound afterward. 
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the flesh and it begins to prick, and bleaches, then you should put the root of the nail under the nail so that it does not hurt the flesh, and push it upward, and cut this flesh subtly and lightly, and put on the remaining flesh medicines burning and corrosive to remove everything; then cure with dressings until it is healed.  
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, so cut it, and treat it well because as long as the bone is corrupted there, it cannot heal; and if you see the two corrode, so cut it in I as we have said before, then cure it until it heals; and if it is broken and hit, and it feels great pain, then you must heal it first; then cut the angle of the spatula sharp by cutting across above, and keep that the cut does not come to the flesh which is below the angle, because the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, so put something on top that soothes. 
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the source from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all flesh, and by chance there is some place where it has bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or where the birth is in some of us the two. 
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in any knot of the thigh does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the thigh, perhaps moves; the size of the one who is fleshy is so light, in such a manner: cut it at its root with a wide spatula. 
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the root of the joint, so is grievous to cure; so keep you from cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In someone who is born or needs the last notch, it is necessary that you first cut the round flesh until the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable size for this one, and then treat it until it is healed. 
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sutures that come as two together come from birth, or from the soldering of a wound, or from the burning of fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary that you cut that suture, so that the parts repair according to their natural forms; then put between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that they do not fuse; or you put between two pieces of thin wood, as long as the edges are soldered, as it is necessary. 
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	The soldering comes to none of his two with the palm, if it copes that soldering as is fitting.
des vils	of the
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large swollen full of melancholic superfluities that come in more members of the body; and more happen in legs of those who go on foot and who work and carry, than others. 
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it behoves you to administer to him once purging of col, and then the salve of basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is in two ways: one is to cut it, and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you open a vein and treat it thoroughly.  
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The thigh is treated in this manner: first, raise the leg in very hot water, until the large vein is softened, then straighten the leg of the patient from above the hip to below the knee; then cut the vein in I place, or II place, or III place, with a wide incision; then release and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the strength of the patient can bear; and then tie it up, and command that he rest on meats avoiding black coal; and resume the evacuation and the salving when the veins are full, and hurt the patient.  
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The elevation of the leg is done in this manner:  Lay the leg of the sick person down, if it has a lot of hair, then put it in water, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red and swells the veins; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by fire, and then cut the vein from the long to the top of the knee, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin with the scalpel and scrape the vein on both sides, until it appears when you feel it; and you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then push the leg down, as long as it is elevated from the skin, and then put it on the splint lightly, then cut in another place above three times; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it with the point, as you did, and put it on another splint, as you did first; then cut another piece, or more if you need it, then lift it, and cut at the top of the foot, then pull and lift until the second piece; then extract by section, as long as it is all released, then cut; and if you cannot pull and raise it, then put a needle in the whole thick double thread, and tie it and pull it, and push it under the tendon, and turn your hand on both sides, as long as it comes out; and guard that it does not break, because if it breaks, you cannot pull nor raise it, and it causes great discomfort to the sick person; and when you have treated it all, put wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound; and care for it until it is healed. 
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron used to strike the vein is curved, and it does not cut, so that it only strikes the vein; and it is of thick curvature, because if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is the shape: 
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein 
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in legs, in warm parts where no grass or tree grows, and in earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it can appear in other places than the legs, and this happens because of rot that comes from beneath the skin, as it comes from within the body serpents and worms, embedded between skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that in the leg there comes a great inflammation, then it changes its color, and begins the vein to flow out, just like the root of a plant.  
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.
