When the shoulder bone opens, it is necessary that you envelop it with a piece of felt from one and a half to two inches, and tie it, and leave the felt on the leg, and every time that it has point at the end, you envelop it around the felt, and tie it; and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and envelop the remaining part, and do not cut it at its root, until it is completely out; for if you cut it, it returns into the flesh, and causes an abscess and decay there, and evil sickness; for that reason, it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the top, and nothing remains on the body; and sometimes this vein when it is treated from five palms of length, or from ten, and one day a man came to me, to whom it came out from ten palms of length, and when you cut it, it puts the bone in view, and pierce it to the bottom, so that all comes out; and be emptied the matter which is inside, and administer to the place medicines preventing decay any day, then treat it as abscesses. 
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes at this vein hand pains, and even when it opens in the joint of the foot, or foot, and there comes much pain, and from which it jumps pains; treat therefore as we have said before. 
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between skin and flesh 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land “disease of the ox,” because it happens many times to oxen, and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down, and one feels it well at the alert of limb in limb, as long as it passes through the skin where it goes, and jumps further; and is engendered by rot of some humors, like come worms and serpents and embers and roundworms of the belly; and one doubts its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it goes up to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times. 
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see him being cured and treated, he cannot be healed except when it comes: so it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong rope very tightly, then cut above and treat the wound, and if the thread goes deep into the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it heals; and the greatest harm that it does is that it corrodes the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or chief near the eye, then restrain below him the eyebrow forming, then cut above, and treat the wound; and it is necessary to use the patient of purification of the body with medicines dissolving for the bad humors poured, and abstain from meats causing putrefaction. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in certain limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you. 
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything else, like live silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and spread to the shoulder, and then shortly after corrupted throughout the body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that it was turning back around her body, as I saw it. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed greatly how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never before seen this illness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I have wanted many to move pain from their place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that this was because the woman had a dry body, and veins discovered, and for that appeared that constrained ventositez; and they do not appear according to this reason to those who are delicious, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.  
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said, then bind above and below tightly, and then cut on top until that windiness is constrained in its place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then cure with those who expel windiness, such as fetid pills, and seraphin pills, and similar others. 
des saiettes	of arrows 
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are some that have large points, and small, and hairy, and joined; and those that have II angles, and those that have tongues, and those where it has pieces; and the one that falls in any member falls according to II manners: or in a principal member like the brain, heart, liver, lung, reins, intestine, bladder, and similar members. 
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls therefore in any place of these members, and the sign of death, that I will tell you after, appear to you: then it is necessary that you desist from the extraction of this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many cases; and when this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not fully embedded, then treat it, and cure the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and leaps the syfac which is above the brain, is when it becomes scotome and sod and overturned and red in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and permixtion of understanding, and vomiting of phlegm; and perhaps without fur from the nostrils, or ears; and perhaps loses speech and voice; and leaps from the wound moist white seeming to poultices, and leaps also as burned flesh; and if this sign appears to you, then hold back from the cure, and treat the arrow if it is not inside.   
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the seventh when it falls or hurts, are that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and by chance the seventh moves also like the arm, and in short black blood comes, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting: know therefore without doubt that death will come. 
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the seventh that does not have a vein is that without any foam jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and gasps loudly and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the hip, it is near the small ribs; and gets great pain and great sorrow and sighing; and they move all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, perhaps something from the undigested flesh leaps from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and nothing of straw comes out through the intestine route, there is no hope for the cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine comes out mixed with blood, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arms and neck and throat and shoulder and auxiliary and spine of the back and groin and hips and legs, and the seeming member, are safe according to more arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for this reason that you do the same thing.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man with an arrow that shot into the root of his nose: I touched it and pulled it out from the other side under the fat of the ear, and it was cured without feeling much.  
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And treat with one game an arrow that it fell in the fat of the eye below the paper below, and the arrow was replaced, and I could not reach but the tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was large as a Turkish bow, to all the iron light without ears; the game was safe, and nothing bad happened. 
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I treated an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I removed the barbs, and carefully extracted it as much as I could, and the Christian became well. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And treated a dart in a man, who had it in his chest or belly, and thought he would die; and then after he had passed thirty days, he did not change his condition; I cut on the dart, and removed it, and pulled it out, and there was no bad accident.  
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if a man has an arrow in his thigh or back, and the wound was sewn shut; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change its natural position, nor finds annoyance in any of its natural works.  
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And there is another man who had an arrow stuck in his face and the wound was closed; and he remained thus suffering great pain; and many other similar things. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated an arrow in the head of the king's man, which was stuck in the middle of his nose, and it was a little bit declining to the right side; and the arrow was completely covered
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow. 
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I felt it with a very fine needle, and did not feel anything; and he felt pricking and pain below his right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on for several days, and sewed up the wound directly, and kept the patient like this for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his body; and he told me so. 
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed on the wound medicine sharp and corrosive for many days, until it was open, and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow which hardened in place; then I adjusted it in the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me; and it stayed well the ends for four months, and then widened so much the wound that I put my forceps in, and the mine from one side and the other, and could not draw it out; therefore I did not cease to devise and engineer instruments in every way, until I took one day the forceps well made, according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, until I drew it out, and restored the wound.  
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physicians judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I then restored it, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was healed entirely. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your care on those that I do not say, because the books cannot take in everything; but the wise masters compare on well little thing, and on those that are present and lacking, find new work, and new instruments, to the descent of strange things that happen in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows are not in members where they are fixed except according to II manners: or by their entry place, or by another part; and the one which is said to be through the place where it enters, is an arrow entering into the flesh, and said to never happen now. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump now, let it remain until the carpus is carried around, and the issue be cleansed; and also if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot exit, let it remain so for some days, and move it each day; and then when it jumps, and if it does not jump, pierce around to all the forest fine, as long as the area around is widened, and then treat it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: do not remove it, but let it stay there until it is equal after some days, because if the arrow comes up to the syfac, it is death.  
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone and does not come to the surface and the patient suffers no ill effects for some days, then the instrument for drawing it out. 
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply lodged and cannot be pulled out easily, then administer poultices as I have told you; then treat the area until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is put back in its place in the body and if one cannot see it, then seek for it with all diligence; and if you feel it, then treat it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot do so because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or vein, then open as much as the wound is large; and treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears by which it is held, then remove the flesh that is attached on both sides to the point that you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as long as you can pull it out; and be careful that you do not break the arrow, that you may pull it out more easily.  
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then lay it until its surroundings are softened, then treat it, because extraction is easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes you go against it, then administer what we have said of the cure in its chapter; and guard yourself from cutting into the nerve and the vein, and put any way that you can move the arrow safely, whether soon or late, whether firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form that he was when the arrow fell into him, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot, then put it according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where one sees nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in that place so that it is visible or felt obviously: cut then above, as much as the pliers can take, and then extract it; if it jumps out now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be drawn out, leave it there still, and then begin the extraction again until it is drawn out; and if the shaft of the arrow is in there, push it out with all the shaft; and if the shaft is fallen, and you see to administer a pushing, then administer the instrument that points enter into the feather of the instrument; and then push further, and if the arrow is feathered, then push the instrument to pointed entry within, so as to ease the extraction. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the wound is surrounded, then it behooves you to cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then cure the wound as it behoves. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls or in the belly or at the bladder or at the ribs, and it is close, and you can cover above, if you cut; and guard yourself from cutting the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound, if need be; and cure until it is healed. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of an eye, and look here at the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many varieties: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is also like that of a bird's feather, to thrust at the tip of the arrow, as it is shaped.  
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tongs for butting and for knowing is here:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins from which one heals, of which there are XVI at the head, that is to say: II battens that are behind the ears, which are called the two "herbech"; and the II arteries that are in the II temples appearing; and II veins that are in the II tear ducts of the II eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the neck; and the II veins that are in the throat; and the II veins that are above the lips, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and II veins that are below the tongue. 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins which one commonly heals are V in each arm: the one is cephalic and is on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "fast", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilica, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly," and is on the fossa, and it is the one which one heals, that opens manifestly above the pouch. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the sap vein is the vein that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and there are two in it; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one of which is below the curve of the pouch of the left rib; and the second sophene which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein that is called «nesse», which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those.  
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bloodletting of the veins that are behind the ears helps with old catarrhs, and migraines; and the quality of the bleeding, as I say to you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient’s neck with a vise, until the two veins appear behind the ears in their two dependences of the head: so aim your knife at the spot where you feel the pulse under your hip, and make an incision there; then take the lancet, and put it under the vein up to the bone, then raise your hand to the whole vein upward, and cut and sever the skin and the vein well two fingers apart, and make blood flow out as much as you see; then strain and bind, until it is cured; and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book. 
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood of the II arteries that are in the II temples, it is good for ancient migraine, and sodden, and accustomed ophthalmia, and to the body of tears sharp to the eyes; and the qualities of the saining are like I say: and it is that the patient strains his neck, as long as the II veins appear openly; and sends the pulse below your right, and then seigne d’enche; then lift the heart above the vein on your right index, and put the lancet below, and lift the vein upward, and the cope, as you have done in the other two veins, and make a correction of blood according to your need; then untie the patient, and put your right upon the vein an hour, then put cotton; and then the ligature forms, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their cut-off and their extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The vein of the front head is as valuable as the cephalic vein for old face diseases, and for migraine, and for redness; and its quality is that the patient strains their neck by twisting it, until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "excavator", whose shape is here: 
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the tip on the vein, and support with your hand, or another thing, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see; then tie the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed and never open it with a wide flame. 
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not proper for the flames to be too large; and to heal across, because the bone is close, and by chance breaks the flames when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of the II veins that are in II tear ducts helps the eyes, and the ear, and the nose, and the pupil in the eye, and diseases of the face; and the qualities of their blood is that the patient pulls his neck twisting from some linen, as before; then the vein, and whether the vein is through, a piece through the long of the flame a piece wide, because there is no flesh. 
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps it breaks; then make a correction of blood, as much as you need it, and then tie up cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein of the nose is good for fever, and for sore throat, and for ailments of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, even when it is old; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient tightens his neck, then strains his nose with his left hand, and takes a fine long flame, and puts it between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well inward, and the person will now begin to bleed; and do not let it go too deep, and make bleed according to your need, then bind it for a night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame: 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the II armpits helps in the treatment of many diseases, such as inflammation, epilepsy, corrosions, and herpes, and scabies. And the qualities of the blood are that the patient strains his neck under both, as we have said; and let the master be standing above the head of the sick person, and the sick person sitting on a seat, then open the vein long and slightly, then draw the blood moderately, or as much as necessary; then make another opening in the other vein, then untie the bandage, and restrain both veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, that the wound may be healed.  
de la sainie des leivres	of the vein of the leaves 
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the lips above helps in collecting in the mouth, and in the corruption of gums, and splits of lips, and sores and ulcers.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the vein are this: make the patient sit in front of you, and restrain his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one is on the right side of the lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by those that are black, and by those that around them there are small black veins: cut therefore both, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest of each part, and also make the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner.  
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the vein under the tongue 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bloodletting of the veins that are under the tongue helps after the bleeding of the cephalic, and it is for the tightening of the throat, and for the diseases of the eye, and for the diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the bloodletting are that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and he raises the tongue, and looks below on each side a black vein:  bleed then one and the other, and do not go too deep, because below are the arteries. 
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins for bloodletting which are commonly used are bled in two ways: either they are pricked with a completely thin flame or with a subtle olive like sharp curettes, and it is called "anesil"; and they are wide and subtle according to the width and thickness of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very well-known, and it is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the veins that are raised plains of thick blood visible, and that contain thick and troubled blood; and this is the form of the olive flame: 
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more subtly pointed, and is for healing veins subtly, where it has subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, so helps with illnesses that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly; and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed skillfully, and that he stay away from the artery which is below. 
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it cuts the earth, and running of blood comes, then it is necessary to cauterize it, as I have said; and it must not be pricking the flame, but cutting like a knife.  
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then it is necessary that you restrain it, and change another; or you wish any vein of it, or you cleanse in its place the vein from the arm: it opens manifestly; and the cut to the flame heals, as we have said. 
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you know the place of the vein, then thus you must draw out the arm so that you touch the place until you know the pulse; then sign the place with ink, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein of the flame anvil; and guard that you do not wound the artery when you see the place inflamed, for it is from the artery: shun it therefore.  
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it rise up as the urine of a child, and the vein is red and subtle, know that it is blood from an artery: hasten then, and place your hand lengthwise above it, then remove your hand if the vein is stained; which happens many times; if you tie up his arm, and leave it so, and do not move it the patient; and be without fear, and do not move it until it is healed. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the limb is not stiff and it pains him, and the medicine is not present to you, then cut the artery if it opens, because the head of the retraction; and stiffen the limb.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a rind of pistachio, and make it split open, and take one of the halves and tie it well up to the other day; if it does not remain unstained, then cure it, as we have said, with powders that staunch blood; and the stanching is not harmful in many dispositions for the small place of the wound, and the strength of the binding of the arm.  
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the arm in the middle is so helpful that it treats blood from above the head, and from below the body, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic, as we have said; and it befits the doctor to place himself toward the nerve which is below, and if it is not too far apart, he finds the nerve, and he inflates it and the saints should be grazed, and by chance may not heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some people because of its subtlety, then you must feel it with the instrument needle; and push the nerve to your power. 
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has a vein between the two nerves, then make a cut along it.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the head so helps that it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; and it is good to bleed them at the olive branch or the myrtle branch, for it is the safest of all veins because it has neither tendon nor nerve nor artery.  
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is necessary to seek the easiest place, and do not worry if it fails the first time, and one begins again; and by chance, it swells the limbs in some men, even if it fails the first time, but it does not matter. 
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing that you must know about bloodletting is that bloodletting is administered only to preserve health and to avoid diseases to come; and let the bloodletting be done in one of the three veins that are or cut: namely cephalic, femoral, and basilica; and one should bleed at the beginning of Lent, during summer and in winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and one should bleed on the first day or the third, after two hours or three days. 
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bloodletting which is administered to the illnesses has no determined hour, but when need is of day or of night, at all hours and in all times; and it does not become to bloodlet children until XIV years, nor women carrying fruit from the first month until the seventh. 
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Do not let them bleed those who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when some want to bleed, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary that they cleanse the intestines with a light enema, if they have much phlegm retained, so that the veins do not attract the superfluous impurities harmful to the principal members; nor let any one bleed who is too full of meat, nor who is drunk, as long as he is so, nor those who are hydrophics; and it is worse to bleed after colic passion, and vomiting, and diarrhea, and multiplication of labor in women, and childbirth, of watching and fasting, and all that which consumes the strength, or by thing of the arm or of the body; then purify the humors, if they are thick, by meat and drinks and medicines, if you have the power; then go into a bath, if nothing forbids it, to purify the blood, and bleed from the vein of the wrist, as we have said; and guard yourself on that day from labor, and pain, and lust, and similar things; and be lying and joyful, and let the one who bleeds be higher than him who bleeds, and rub the arm two or three times, then tighten the ligature above the middle, because when it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct the blood; and then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell and are felt; then moisten the bleeding point of a little old oil, then place the tip of your left hand over that vein below the wound an inch or where you want to bleed, so that the vein does not move and be cut by the iron. 
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that go as if cords to the groin, and some are full of windiness, so that when one puts on the flame, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these; and if one opens the vein, then the wound is too tight, therefore it behooves that the veiners be warned about these things. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; if not, it begins again a little below where it was previously, as long as the lesion is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is swollen, and the patient is afraid, let him leave it for one or two days, and do not bandage his arm: perhaps there will come boils; nor enter into a bath, then resume bleeding if he wishes; and if the wound is small, or the vein is subtle, and you doubt that it isn't as much blood as you see, pierce in that same wound directly to the entire flame; and work a point gently, so that the limb be swollen; for this often happens, when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place inflamed, do not begin the vein again, and put on a little bit of oil, for it thickens the body of blood and is mixed in this place with the oil; and so administer the oil in each vein that you drain the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same thing applies to triacle and butter of eggs, when it is put on the place; so subtly the pain and it separates when it is too large. 
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, even when it is only drained once or the opening of the vein is small, hasten and place on top a sponge moistened in water and a little warm, and restrain for an hour; and you must do this after the discharge of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after several days without any blackness or greening, it will not harm him; and if you see it, put on top nothing of aloes or myrrh mixed with juice of calamine, monuments, or similar.  
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearance appear at the shrine of the basilica: put therefore your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, then is that appearance evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore shun that you put on anything of those we have said, for by chance it may be without the artery; but make one plaster dry to harden the place, then heal with another cure, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each according to the quantity of their virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it ooze until it is red; and if you see it swollen, let it subside until it is thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is stout and strong, and has need of bloodletting, to make a wider wound, and let the flames be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed him little and often, and he should be bled by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of bleeding is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and is more useful than bleeding through long or wide. 
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to the one whose body needs to be bled, it is necessary to give softened bread in pomegranate juice; if it is warm, treat them with blood III times or IV. And if it is of cold complexion, before bleeding, soften bread in quince syrup, or in honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chicory, and a well-smelling syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it pricks at the vein, after the issue of much blood, then it is necessary that he moisten broth of meat, and subtle fragrant syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of the vein. 
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to drain his arm, and bleed another time, if it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to drain his arm after the first bleeding, and he has strong flesh, he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to bleed from another place, they must bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Because there is much blood within the body which has already been weakened and causes fever; so it is necessary to milk a large quantity, and widen the wound as much as it falls into a poultice; then that you reward all the conditions of health, and put your hand upon his arm when he is healthy, that death may not come in place of the poultice, and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent; and it does not behoove you when you see to untie his arm, and let blood a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press strongly upon it; nor if it is curved, that he extend his arm as far as possible, for that would be bad; but leave it so long as it heals a second time; or that you point at the tip of the flame, until the blood which is frozen to the vein of the wound has issued forth, and put upon I place of the poultice in a pointed form, and press lightly. 
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not constrict it at all, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is a need to draw blood the second time, let it be drained in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein to draw blood from the arm is located in the place of the vein at the head for that reason she is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the vein is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the bone is red; then it should be bound moderately so that the vein appears well, then it should be cut through the width, neither wide nor long; and the opening should be wide, and the incision made close to the joint of the hand, and if he cannot pull out anything, put the hand back in hot water, and leave the blood in the water until you have enough; and if it is in summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, for one puts it in more in winter than in summer; and the vein of this vein is safer than all other veins, because there is no artery or nerve. 
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The blood of the salve of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: strain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein swells, if one can see it; and if the vein is crooked, and if you cut it all through, it does not harm anything; and do not let it go too deep, because the nerves are under all the skin, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot exit. 
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, then place oil and wool on top of the vein to soothe it, and do this for each one.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein of the left hand is as good for the disease of mice, and do everything just as I have told you about the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the sophene is good for all illnesses that are below the body, such as diseases of the legs, and retention of flowers, and illness of the hips, and thighs and old leg pains, and similar illnesses. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of his healing are that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it becomes numb, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many veins; heal therefore where more wide vein, or at the ankle, which is worth. 
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you drain it above the foot, guard yourself from the nerves that are below, and drain it transversely as well when cutting; and let the flame be annealed.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot insert it, put the foot back in water, and allow the vein to drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the first time it fails, begin again from above a little higher, because the place is salty. 
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle of fire, and its puncture is worth to the pain of the hip when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the qualities of its vein is that the patient enters into a bath, and he pulls up above the ankle IV fingers twisting, because otherwise it doesn't open the vein; and if it opens, you cleanse the vein in all the ways that you can, and traversing; and it is better that you cut it, because the skin is dry, and it is very well recovered by the hands of man. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it [the dislocation], search any vein of the one who opens or back of the foot, and towards the small thigh, and guard the nerves; and make so much correction of blood as you see, and then untie the bandage, and put cotton on top and bind it; she is now healed. 
des sainies de ventouse	of the suction cups  
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Sucking blisters are made of horns, or glass, or wood; and suction is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is felt to be harmful is according to II manners: either it is all fire or without fire; and cupping that is done by hitting and by the extraction of blood is done in XIV places of the body, of which one is entirely on the head; and the other is in the neck; and II others in II ribs of the neck; and the cup under the chin; and the cup on the II shoulders; and the cup above the hips; and the cups between the II arms; and the cups on the II legs; and the cups on the II ankles; and cupping does not treat blood, except for the small veins that are spread throughout the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken as one does from bloodletting of a vein; and it should not be administered, neither all fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied.  
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of maladies it is necessary to bleed, or for customs, then we must bring them each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in every time; for there are such that, when they have need to bleed, they have a heavy head; and there are those who have swelling and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and darkness in their eyes; and some who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and have inflamed the tongue, and cough up blood; and there are such who dream, and see through blood and corpses and deaths and similar things.  
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is emitted from the month, we command to ventilate after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bloodletting of the vein helps with the great pain of the head... that comes to the eyes, and it is not fitting that this be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventosation is in place of the bloodletting of the cephalic, and it is not fitting for those who are of cold complexion to use it, or who have phlegm, because this does great discomfort to them; and therefore it is not fitting for the elderly to use it, nor those who have or chief colds maladies.  
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal with this, often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to place the suction cup a little lower due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation of the neck is in place of the vein of the head and the basilica, and for this reason it is good for the treatment of the foot, and for opening the channel of the groin, and to all, and to repletion; and it is necessary to put a little, because if it is held too tightly, it can cause blockage in the stomach or heart. 
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilations at the II ribs of the neck are good for pains in the head, and headache, and migraine, and for strangulation, and for pain at the roots of the teeth, and is in place of the vein of the basilica; and it is necessary that you command the patient to spread his hand when putting it on, so that he does not cut the artery, and does not have a hemorrhage. 
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The venting under the chin is good for mouth ailments, and gum rot, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for illnesses that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The incisions of the veins are worth as much as three veins in the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient not to feel them too deeply, because their skin is bare and lies near nerves and arteries. 
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup which is on the rump is good for hemorrhoids of the base, and for diseases of below, and it is necessary that the suction cup be large, and be of iron, that she has need to well suck; and perhaps, if she were thin, she would break; and in this I make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups of the legs are helpful, because they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the hips, and of the knees, and of the bladder, and relax the flowers; and are in their place at the .ij. shins, and the .ij. ankles, and all the same they weaken the body after long use, and bring weakness in more dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting the suction cup is that you put it first empty, and suck temperately, and put it steadily, and move equally, and do not cease doing this, until you see the place red and inflamed, and appear the color of blood; then finish, and put back the suction cups, and take ward in the disposition of the body, because there are such who have tanned flesh, and clear pores: so it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, then it is necessary to prick twice: the first time to gently open the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, then it is necessary to prick a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, then we only prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much blood, let us often return; and if the veins are thick, let them be made thinner by fire, and the ends so that the veins are pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those who have thick skin and hard, and who have bad pores, that you grease their places with cupping glasses of oil appetizer and dissolving: if it is in summer, of violet oil, or almond oil, or oil of squash seed; and if it is in winter, of cresson oil, or lilies, or chamomile, or something similar. 
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, then take wormwood oil, or balm, or anise oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.
