And if the one who is being treated has taut skin and large pores, one must not put any oil on it, but one must wash it after the ventilation of rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of gourd, or water of porcelain, or something similar. 
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, rises from ease with myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have gross superfluities let themselves rise from old wine, or from their own water, or from a decoction of anise or chamomile, or others like; and it is not fitting to suck before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath an hour or II; and do not sleep after the suction, and it is necessary that he be warmed, when it is due to be suctioned and when it is suctioned. 
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard him who is well-tempered with jaundice, and if his blood is too thick and inflamed; then he should eat cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces at the meal, and similar things; and quince seeds, and roasted meat, and moist meats. 
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, let him take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and menjuce poc, and menjuce pucins and small birds and pigeons; and on the day that he will be vented, he must drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men triacle or musk before or after the venting, to comfort the principal members; and be subtle the sans, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it. 
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are applied without harming are those that are placed on the liver and the spleen and gout and on the belly and the flank and the hips and the groin because these members do not suffer from being hurt on their own, and it is done only to draw blood from member to member as when we put them on the breasts when the milk comes in; to remove the viscosity that is in the member as when we put suction cups on the belly and the flank to reduce the limb; and to remove pain when there is an obstruction or stone, since by its attractive virtue it may perchance remove the obstruction, or dislodge the stone from its place; and so it does when one puts it on the liver and the spleen when there is retained windiness, and these suction cups are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and some times filled with warm water, as in diseases of the pleura, and in this way one fills the suction cup with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs suitable for it have been boiled. 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should have two arms of a width and half palm in length, and have on the side around the middle a small hole, as if to put a needle, and be of iron, soft before so that it does not prick the patient when putting it on the limb; and have in the middle a bar of iron or steel, to put a burning candle, and let them be large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them; because the suction cups of children are other than those of old people, and of the thin ones compared to the fat. 
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must thus put this suction cup onto the limb: take the candle of wax or linen, and place it inside the suction cup along with the shaft that is within the suction cup, so that the brightness is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient; and then place it on the limb, and the ends must be on the openings that we have said, so that when one wants to, vapor goes in, and one removes the suction cup; and take the linen as before, and repeat often, if you have need. 
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup which is administered in the illness of pleurisy, in all acute cases, it has no handle or opening, and it is not administered unless it is full of water, and it is placed on the limb only so much; and this is the form: 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leech are brought into use only in members where one cannot apply leeches because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar; and in the fleshless places of them, such as two or three, and other similar; and the quality of using it is that when you find leeches that are in clean sweet water without being purged, take them; and put them in a nut in fresh water until they become plump, and have nothing in their bellies; and then let the member be bled and have a cupping glass applied, then rub the limb until it becomes red, and put the leeches on top; and when they are full and fall off, if there is a place where you can apply a cupping glass, apply one, because this is of great benefit. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If it is not so, if you raise the place of ash, and then of water, very well, and then the sprint; and if the part heals too after the body of the wounds, if you wet a cloth of linen in cold water, and put above, as long as the wound is stretched; and if the wounds are multiplied, if you put above vitriol ground, or gale, and similar things, as long as it is stretched; or you put on the place half of peeled beans, and leave them until they are dried on the place, now it will stop; and if you need more of it, if you take other wounds.  
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the sutures will not be taken, then rub the place with fresh blood, or pierce it with a needle until the suture comes out, and then put them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will harden; and when you see that they are coming out, powder them with a bit of aloes and silk ground, or ash, they will now hold. 
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoring of fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear friend, that the foolish mire themselves in this chapter so they never see any of the ancient books, nor read a letter from them; and for this cause is the science restrained in our land, because I never found any good one; and I know nothing, except by the science of the ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have shown you here in this chapter what is contained, and have abridged it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I have done in these II chapters before. 
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It behooves us therefore to say or prologue of this book the sum of the word and chapters where the sages put his understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and learn it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient on one side and the other, if nothing hinders it, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age; or if his temperature is not very warm, or too cold; and avoid cold things, that is to say, cold meats, and meat of deer and lamb, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not overfill yourself with meats which fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of a hot abscess, or spreading of matter in the limb; then return the patient to his former rule that he has used. 
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meats that make great nourishment, or have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and testes, and pies, and belly of beef, and eels, and fresh fish, and red wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment they regain strength and the fracture heals faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones broken in the old and the decrepit do not well take back nor solder according to their nature for the dryness of the members, nor those also who are too tender, like the bones of little children; but no care, reset on the broken bone I great tendons which hold together and join the limb together, as long as it forces so as it was before; and not at all point of its work, and for this you must nourish them with big meats, as we have said. 
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg or foot, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the side and another that goes to a point, like the point of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if with fracture, and fracture to a small crack entirely.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And to each manner has its instrument, and its own tool in the restoration, according to what the memory comes into its place; and is known the fracture of the bone by those that the leg is twisted, and opens well by exterior, and hurts at the pressure of the hand; and when there is no torsion nor hurt at touching, and the patient does not feel much pain, if there is no fracture; but it may well have torsion, or fissure, or small fracture. 
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you should not move it by hand, but put on the remedies that come after here, and then restrain it carefully.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that goes in arc, and are the II parts disjointed, it is necessary now to put them equally well, so that abscesses do not come; and if abscesses come, let him leave for no day, until the abscesses be appeased; then he puts it equal to the flesh that you can easily and wisely, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration of this one where there are pieces; then restrain, as it is convenient after. 
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone is broken in pieces, if it's of two parts, if it's hands or feet, or to your hand if it's a small limb, or if it's two cords, or if it's one cord and to your hand; and put the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, you reset by all means the additions in their places as much as you can, and keep that by your work does not come to the patient lesion nor pain; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms. 
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels it well in the hand if it seems to you that it is not well: if it is arranged nicely, and do not restrain it too much, nor press as those who make it come by their work abscess hot and contraction to the limb, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, carefully instruct the patient not to move it, neither when awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way; and guard well that the limb be so secure that it feels no pain. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, except at a point, and it is necessary to put him in such a position that he feels no pain; and keep him straight so that no tortuosity comes when he is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you. 
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs, and similar: it is necessary to envelop them with soft and thin linen cloths; and those which are large, such as hips and legs: it is necessary to envelop them in a wide and hard bandage, because the wide bandages embrace the whole great limb, and restrain it from all sides equally, so that there is no tear; then bind around light splints, III tours or IIII according to the limb, and strain one hand a little at all the bandage, then go above the fracture and strain less, than the fracture then moves away a little from the fracture; and soften the bandage little by little, until you reach a great part of the healthy place, then take the other bandage, and turn around again straight above the fractured place; then return to the lower part of the fracture, and strain moderately, not too much nor too little, as we have said in the first place above; then put between the bandages splints of linen or cloths, so that it be all equal, then tie everything on top with a bandage, and then put your well-made pads on top, if there is no abscess or swelling. 
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an inflammation or abscess, put a soothing poultice upon it, which takes away the inflammation, and leave it so for some days; then strain the edges of the wound together, and let them be of half a palm's breadth well-set, or of staff from which one makes staves, or of palm branches, and let them be according to this figure: 
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the splint that one puts upon the fracture be a little larger and wider than the others; and also as long as it is convenient to the limb of smallness or greatness; then bind upon the splints just as you have done at the first layer, then tie above with a thread evenly, just as in the first layer upon the fracture; more strict is above, less below; and it is necessary that the thread be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen; for if the thread are thick, as I want works of the fools who make their bandages with cords of twisted linen, and this is a great error, because the bandage cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and it does not behoove that there be between each splint less than two fingers' width of space. 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is irritated by the edges of the stars after the tightening in their healthy places, then put under them pads of linen or wool felt so that it does not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a break and the tendons are broken, I will say about its cure here after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not fitting to set all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it does not suit to put splints, because after V days or VII, or more according to your certainty of abscess, it heals; and see here the manner of the ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and that you take flour that holds on the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and put this mixture, not too light nor too thick, and use, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring the fracture in more dispositions, and also to women and to small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.  
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take  three pieces of ginger, laudanum, nutmeg, asafoetida, and Arabic gum and myrrh and aloes, each  five; alechil eight, and make it into powder, and mix it with a good amount of egg. If the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth to more men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of plaster that is good for torsion: take mugwort and marshmallow, ana X З.; myrrh and aloes, ana VIIII З.; acacia VI З.; Armenian bole X З., and grind well, and confit with water or the white of an egg, and administer. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another manner of plaistering joints and bones dislocated from their places, and soothing the pain that comes, and the use of the bone, and the fracture: take new linen, and moisten it in wine and oil cooked, and put it on the place.  
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore [anything], but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and removes properly the pains. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of ointment which restores broken bones: take dry fig leaves, and earth laurel leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of splinting for the restoration of a broken bone and to lessen the remainder of the abscess. 
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of marshmallow, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of chickpeas, one part each; and grind, and boil with wine, and if the limb is chilled, boil it with moist coriander water, or water, and use. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another manner of setting a bone more forceful than the first, when an abscess comes hard to the restoration of the limb. 
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of vismalve, and seeds of flax, balm, melilot, and wormwood, and flowers of violets and camomile, each one part; and grind, and confit with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its repose. 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Galen says in his book that one should put on the broken limb for restoration only a certain thing made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and that it should be between two soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen that one must put upon the broken limb, to restore, things dry a little warm, like myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of making an ointment that is good for the injury and pain: take mugwort and chicory of men chopped, or feathers of bird, and wormwood, and equal parts, and grind them, and make it into an ointment and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then you unbind it a little after, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor have the bones moved from their place; if he does not unbind for many days And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or inflammation, then hasten, and unbind it, and remove the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and sponge of sea moist, and dip in water, and raise the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on a dry cloth, half in water or in rose oil, and tie above a nut, as long as you are sure of a hot abscess; and rest the inflammation of the member, and be removed the pain, then begin again the subtle ligature, and a little of plaster, and do not bind it so tightly as before; and subtilize until it is healed. 
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is closed and red and pain and swelling are entirely gone, and you have need of plaster and linen, then begin again as you did at first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb any of what we have said, then do not unbind it before III days or IIII or V or VII; and at no time leave it XX days, according to what one sees, until the fracture heals, and approaches the adjustment of the bone on top; therefore restrain it more than first, and it makes its flesh grow, as I said before; and if you see it drying more than is necessary, know that there cannot come nourishment; arose then the hot water from bath, all times that you unbind it, and this be each third day, and slacken a little the ligature; by this work therefore shortens the nourishment to the limb, and amends hastily those who do foolishly, who leave the limb crooked: this is evil, and so is the work dangerous, and I see no other thing than to let it dry and to operate it straight. 
des diverses manieres de brisure	of diverse ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of fractures, and various figures, and the causes are determined; for there are fractures that are made by the thrust of a sword, and the collarbone breaks all the bone up to the shaft which is below the bone, such as it is made high or fast; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called "haichure". 
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing, and this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; and is the wound of these two fractures large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or splitting or of the collarbone of stone, or of the cheek on stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture penetrating, which approaches to the skin that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound which is put back in the bone as subtly as a horsehair, and the fissure is small, and for this reason this fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound which is made either by striking of stone, or by falling, or by something similar, and makes the piece of bone go inside, and its legs are like how the blacksmiths do when they strike on the cauldrons; so it goes between the pieces. 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have or chiefs moist bones, such as children's heads; and it happens in all these ways of fracture that small pieces are broken off from them such as stars; and I will speak of it in its place. 
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of fractures by the retraction on them, and the examination of tendons, and by the corrupted cartilage that is on top.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of capillary blood is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubs on it, the black fracture appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of the fracture, take heed of the accidents of the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of phlegm, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and eyes staring and reddening, and other similar things in more dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an escapable accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the broken bone first comes to you, and it is in winter, then it behooves you to remove the bone before the fourteenth day, as much as you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue under the bone may not rot and bring about the accident that we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture comes to the membrane that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you split the broken part as follows: and it is that you prick the head of the patient deeply, and uncover on the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more carefully than you can, and if bleeding comes out when uncovering the bone, or abscess apply, then help him with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the place with dressings soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess has calmed down, and be assured of the bleeding; then begin to remove the bone, and this is done in two ways of work: one way is that you cut at a narrow width in front, and this is the form:  
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make one other incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have a number of incisions of various sizes, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and made of iron, and in working lightly, so that you do not cut the bone.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and out, then it behooves you to pierce it through, so that you administer splints with drill bits, not more than that lest they pierce beyond the bone of the test, and must have above the point a margin or a circle, which does not allow the point beyond the bone; and you should have several more, so that each comes in its place to the width of the bone, so that you have drill bits for all tests; and this is the form of the three kinds of splints:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing through the broken bone are that you put one drill bit on the bone and turn with your hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then put the drill bit elsewhere a little after, and so do all around, then cut with the cutting instruments the space of the bone which is between the holes, and do this more subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have like tweezers, pliers; and guard that you do not touch the brain nor the dura mater.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you will have pierced the bone, and treated it, it is necessary that you remove the appendage which is stayed from the bone to all other instruments similar to a scalpel, but it is necessary that it be more firm and more subtle than the other scalpel; and if there remains anything of the small bones, or no scales, then the oste lightly to the instruments; then cure the wound of tents and ointment as we have said. 
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of work is that which Galen says, which is drier; and he praises it much, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture appears open, so that when you have uncovered that part, then you place beneath the head of this lens-shaped incision tool, for this is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut in one direction, and is the part sharp in two sides, so that the cutting edge is toward the bone; then strike with a small mallet above, so that you lightly break the bone all around, and take good care of the membrane that is below; if it adheres to the bone, then gently lift it off, because one should lift it without discomfort, and without fear. 
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not reach the skin, and the bone is broken only from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to remove that asperity and remove the scales with a fine razor, of which you must have various quantities, in order to administer in each place the most suitable one, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you begin with large razors, and afterwards with finer ones, and do not cease until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other capillary cuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary that you administer the cause according to its placement; and this thing is not returned to him who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is uncovered, it behooves you to take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and put it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and put it on top of the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, that you do not burden the wound, then administer from above another linen bandage, and do not tighten it more than necessary to keep the wound alone; and let it remain like this for a day or two, until the abscess has subsided, then untie it, and administer medicines such as the roots of lilies, and wheat flour, and incense powder, and arnica, and similar things; and of these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and administer further medications unmixed with mordants; and keep that the wound is always clean, so that you do not leave any ointment there, nor allow any scab to gather, because when a scab gathers on the brain cloth, it will corrupt and rot, and bring great evil to the patient; because when one puts mordant things on the wound, they will fester from above.  
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take ward then, if any bad accidents come to the patient, as we have said, so is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blackening does not come from outside except for the medicine that has been put on it, that it may have virtue, then you must take a part of honey and III parts of rose oil and glue I drapel and put it on the scab; then cure in ways of cures as it is necessary, until it is healed. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that no times are broken the two parts of the two above, or one by the alone, because they are two bones; and this below is cartilaginous, and does not break at all, if not forced to bend or twist, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you put your small finger or a hole in them, and place each fracture inside your index finger, and to the palm outwards, until the bones return according to their natural shape; and do this gently, and guard that the patient does not feel pain from your work. 
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the knee, and it cannot come to its place, then you must put it even at the head of a stick somewhat thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is of II parts, make another one, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscess has calmed down, then bind it with two tents of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part.  
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind one on the other side, if the fracture is there; and let the thicknesses be so thick that they fill the hollows of the knee.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And certain restorers say one must moisten the tents in butter, and change each day. 
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be softened in the making of auburn from an egg, and ground flour; then leave the tent, as long as the bone is hard, and the cartilage hardened.  
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one puts in their place goose feathers instead of tents, and so with i.e. one sheet of cloth wrapped around it, and holds the bandage, and breathes the patient amongst; do as you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if the abscess comes to the new ones while you are working on it, if you put cerote or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in one poke of diachylon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come not, put a plaster from outside, of sesame flour, and incense powder, conﬁted with egg white, then put light dressings on top, and do not bind them in any way; and if the fracture of the bones is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract it with suitable instruments for this, then sew the fissure, and cure it with things like bandages and ointments that are suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside the bone, then cure it with tents, and put splints on them, until it is healed. 
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the jaw fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken below and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is outside only so much, and is not broken in two, except that it buckles inward, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right part, that you put your index finger into the mouth of the sick person; and if the fracture is in the left jawbone, then put your index finger of the right hand, and push the fracture inward lightly, and fix it with the other hand from outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is separated in two, it is necessary that you administer extension of two parts, until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or a rupture, so restrain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the broken jawbone cerote, and put on i drapel double; and put on the drapel a great estele well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the mandible, and tie it up as much as you can, and command the patient to rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, so untie it on the third day, and then reset what is changed; and put a plaster on top, of powdered mill with an abundance of egg or sesame flour, after which you have removed the cerote; and put on top of the plaster light linen, and if the plasters dry up, and the disposition of the patient does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy; many times it is healed in 3 weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, so administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reward no piece of bone has been removed; so subtly of the bone with instruments suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, so enlarge it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, so close the wound, if it is wide, and put upon it one plaster suitable for this, to hinder flesh, until it be healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fracture breaks many times in front, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is according to three manners: or it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is like this when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder which is the broken bone; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put each of the fractures to your hands, so that the form be as it should be, and there be neither appearance nor blemish.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it more, so put under the shoulder of the patient a round sphere of cloth, or wool, and be thick according to your need; and gently lift the bone, and hold the sphere with your hand, so that you put each of the fractures as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder back with force because it comes in front, then it is necessary that the patient lie often on his side, and put under the shoulder one hour glass, and push the minister's shoulder down, until the bone of the shoulder be lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture to your two sides, and if you find it fractured, then it is necessary that you split above; and treat the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join by any mounting, then cut at one of the incisors that you have; but that you put under the shoulder this instrument, in order to guard against displacement:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and seems like a spoon, and is not too deep, and be as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and have two handles, as you see, and one broad, and the other narrow, as is the rupture of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are assured of a hot abscess, so close the wound, and if the rupture is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, so cover the wound with drapes and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, then moisten one cloth in rose oil and honey and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The tightening of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you put on the bone the plaster of the powder of the mill and of white of egg, and put light pads on top, and put a spear under the armpit, if you have need; then take a very large bandage of one palm wide, then put the double drape above the pads and the plaster; then take a strip subtle of III two wide and long, and wrap it around that bandaged, so that the head of the bandage be hanging down; and put the strip on the fracture, and turn the bandage around the neck, and under the good armpit, and under the bad armpit; and tighten each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the strip does not move above the broken bone, so reward it every day, and when the ligaments loosen, then restrain it; and make the patient lie on his back, and put him when he sleeps the small pillow under the armpit, to raise the shoulder up; so alleviate the fracture of the shoulder by relieving the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless a bad accident happens, until XX days; then renew the plaster, if you see that it needs it, and restrain and leave it so, until it is restored; and it is restored at most in XXVIII days, and less in some men. 
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It sometimes happens that the shoulder breaks or is dislocated in the middle, and it should only be moved with touch; then arrange according to the shape of the break, and reset according to its natural form, in all ways that you can; then place on the wound powder from the mill with an abundance of egg, and light bandages, and put on top a double cloth. Then place on top a wide and thin splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the splint is hitting in any part of the shoulder, so use linen bandages to cover it, so that the splint lies evenly; and then tighten it with a very firm bandage, so that the splint does not move from its place, and look at the wound every day; and whenever it softens, tighten it, and place the splint straight if it is out of place, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in twenty days or twenty-five, And when this number is completed, then untie it, and be sure, for it is not bone that easily comes loose.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone has gone forward and is not below the heart, then do as follows, and apply the bone, and do what we have said in the break of the collarbone to soothe an abscess hot.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the end.  
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken within, it sinks down to the back, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of strength, and all things, and perhaps vomits blood, and opens the seams in the broken bone, and he feels them well. 
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and put one cushion between the shoulder blades, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the sides of the two bones with your hands, and skillfully brings them together in all ways that you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then put plaster and bandages above the fine layer of salt, or some other light paste, and wrap it in one cloth, and tie it on the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the band around the back, and restrain it firmly, and reward every hour the bandage, and if it loosens, tighten it; and if it needs to be untied, for corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, hasten then, and untie it, and remove what has come from the bandages, and address those things in ways of healing; then reapply the bandage, and restrain it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs comes only in their thick parts after the back, and at the head within, and they bend only for that reason because they are glassy; and one feels it well upon inquiry on the two sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoring is that you put equal the fracture, as it convenes.  
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put the splint on it, and restrain it with a band, if you need it. 
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is leaning inward, the patient feels very great pain and pricking, as well as from pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; and also pains, and coughs and vomits great plants of blood, and this is of grave health, and the ancients have placed great engines upon it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is necessary to administer meats that swell the belly, to bring the rupture to the outside.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except for hot abscesses if they have not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, then treat it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that some put suction cups on the spot to suck out  fluids, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the suction cup pulls out superfluities to the spot for the arrangement of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say of you it must cover the place with wool dipped in hot oil, and put a tent between the ribs to make the flesh equal, then be cured from the cure of pleurisy, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot suffer because of the bone that pricks the skin, and there is doubt for the patient, then it is necessary to split on the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put under a tool to ward the face; and afterwards one must cut the bone, and drain gently, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with ointments, until it is healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, put on it moist cloths in rose oil, and put on top of that; and cure while the place where it is appropriate for the abscess, and lying still on its side or where it should be, until it is healed.  
de la brisure dou col	of the break of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a fracture occurs in the bones of the neck, and sometimes it happens that it bends; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, if you take notice if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many cases, and if they move and feel well when pulled and held still, know that the bone's articulation is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if one puts care into it.  
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is sound or not, then take ward if the limbs are softened, and if the accidents are who are in hands, and on the back there is buoyancy and ejection without volition; and when one has supported it on its belly, then there is ejection without volition. 
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is set on its back and it wants to sit down, it cannot. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: if one does not labor in its cure. 
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward it if there is an abscess hot, so put on the spine rose oil or oil of egg yolk, until it is appeased; then put on a comforting and drying plaster, and tie it with a band, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, as long as he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bones are dislocated, it is necessary to cover the wound; and remove the bone, then assemble the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with one suture, then cure it with ointment inhibiting flesh, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow," then put your fist from your left hand into it, and set it equal to the other hand in your power, then put on the plaster and splint on top, if you need it; then restrain it, and if there are bones dislocated, do this, remove the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Sometimes it happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it happens, it has not happened from a little weakening at the top; and making long, and declining to the side, and comes to the patient pain in the place, and tingling, and swells what breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, as much as you are on the fracture; and know which is the fracture and the figure of it; and if the fracture is at the top only, put equal to this fracture, as long as it is in a natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it declines to the inside, put the patient on his belly, as long as the restoration of this fracture becomes apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you would have it even, put it upon the splint, then put upon a strip of wood or of bark, and restrain the splint so that it does not move; and apply the place under the ribs, as long as the limb is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep upon his healthy side or upon his back.
