Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes to it, do not touch it until the abscess has subsided, and put upon it what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and restrain it as it is fitting, if there is no bad accident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the elbow and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two ways: one of which is that you take one stick of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two heads of two ropes together, and lift them up, and place the patient on one seat; then place his broken arm on top of the stick, as far as it comes to the armpit, and make a curvature in the stick, then put on any heavy thing or minister's extend it down; then put the patient's fracture equal to his hands together, until the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one supports the patient on his stretcher and ties his hand to his neck, then instructs two ministers that one holds what is above the fracture in his hands, and the other holds below by about a foot, and extend each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more difficult, hold the linen beneath and above the fracture, and extend each minister to its side.  
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the shoulder, it is necessary to put one linen below the armpit and the other towards the side, below the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the side, then it is necessary to put the linen gently, without labor, until the fracture is equal on top and on the side; then set the fracture as it should, and restrain it, if an abscess does not come. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess does come there, do not restrain it until .vij. days, and put on linen half in oil and rose oil, until the abscess has calmed; then restrain it, and the manner of restraining it is that you place the plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the drape, and restrain on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm be in its place of stars, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone moves, use splints, and put on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint .i. two of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes over the fracture .iij. two on each side; then restrain on the splints, in the same way as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the fracture, more strongly and less by moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the setting of the bones, and the tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess hot, so leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then look every three days the binding, that itching or inflammation does not come to the place, or the suppurations cannot come to the limb for because it is too far. 
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said. 
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents come to pass, then he should not untie it except after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach; and put under the shoulder one cushion full of wool evenly, and look every hour of the day or from the nut, that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or the ligaments are softened; if it advances by the virtue of medicine, and give him the food that we have put forward, in such a way that the meat is at first subtle; and when he begins to recover, let it be coarse. 
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be taken back in forty days from the whole; and therefore one must loosen and administer bath and medicines of emollient for the place to be bettered. 
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and crowded, it stays untied for days or months.  
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of .ij. bones, which are called the two "fossil," because one is small, and that follows the socket; and the other is large, and that is below, towards the little toe; by chance breaks the large fossil alone, or the small, and by chance and both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; and when the large ones are broken, the healing is bad, and more grievous than when they are broken together.  
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that is broken alone, then it is necessary to gently extend it and make it equal. 
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the great fossa, then it must be pulled more strongly; and extend above the cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small fingers lower than the other fingers, and let the patient be crossed upon himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient suffers no labor; then extend the ministers' arms to the part below his hand, or at the limb, and one other minister on the other above. 
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the mirrors equal, according to its best form. 
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is any dislocated that pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make it as above with the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; so take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of restoring abscesses arise, then glue a plaster made of rose oil and white wax, that it be neither too hard nor too soft; and lay the plaster above subtly, until the abscess is calmed. 
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then the osteopath removes the cerote, and he puts in the emplastrum of powder from the mill with abundance of egg, then he puts the splints, and let the splint of the fracture be close more outwards, and a little wider than the others; and know that it must have six splints or arms in more dispositions: whether the fracture is in one of the bones, or two; and restrain more over the fracture than elsewhere, and all days less distancing, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths which are over the splint be soft and moist, and be not hard nor rough; and let the thread, with which it is restrained, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.  
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the limb after several days.  
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you raise the limb in hot water, until the itching be appeased; and let the limb not rest at all. 
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the tightening, and if the ligaments are loosened and the bones are dislocated, and similar things, so the address. 
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care that the nourishment cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, then it is necessary that you soften it a little, and leave it so for some days, until the nourishment returns, and then restrain it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said comes to the patient, do not unbind him until twenty days. 
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or when he is turned around, then let him put his hands on his neck, and be his neck equal, and guard against movement and agitation, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues. 
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and among us there are few fractures, and it comes but rarely many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or sprained, it behooves the patient to sit crossed and straight before him equally; then put his hand on the board stretched out, and extend the ministers the broken bones, and place them equal in size, until they are well joined; and put the plaster and bandages, if an abscess does not come, then put a splint according to the quantity of the place; and be wrapped in .i. linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is at the base toward the belly of the palm, make a ball of cloth and command the patient to tighten it on his broken palm; then strain it with a long cloth, and let the splint be as hard as the palm of the hand, and strain it, as it behoves.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the outside, it behooves you to put a splint above and another below in the plant, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand and close the connection between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of the two bones, if it is a pouch, put it equal, as it behooves; and restrain it with the plant, and if you see fit to put a small straight splint to raise the fracture, and not move; and if the fracture is in the other bones, such as in the index or one of the others, put it equal, and tie it with the healthy bone which is after; or you tie them all in one holding, that it moves well, or you put a splint on top, like a pouch; and take care in the restoration and disposition of an abscess, hot, and dry what comes from it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the hip is many times broken, and one sees it well when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is so-and-so, that is, one above the fracture, and one below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then extend each minister his limb to his equal part; and this is when the fracture is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the hip, one ligament should be pulled towards the groin, and the other ligaments below the fracture. 
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, and then the ligaments are around the knee, and the extension below; then put the hands to the bone equal with their two hands, as long as it is according to its natural figure, and then put the splint, and the bandage, if there comes an abscess. 
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess hot, let it be soothed then return to your work and your treatment; the bandage is made in such manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the broken leg with a hard bandage doubled in II or III, and remove the superfluities, then turn the leg so that the heels reach to the root of the thigh, and put long thread between the hip and the leg, below the knee, and let the end of the thread go up; then turn back on the leg and on the hip the bandage, then put above the fracture splints, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then employ the place eight between the leg and the hip of cloths soft to put equal the tightening, then begin to tie firmly III turns or IIII on the fracture; and as much as you go up on the fracture, and less the constraint; then take the two ends of the thread that you have put between the hip and the leg, and tie III splints that are above, then return down to the end of the thread, until you reach near the foot; and tighten, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it so, then lest there comes a suppuration or swelling or any other semblance. 
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, let him untie it, and address those that come, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that pinch, it is fitting to extract them, if one can; and if one cannot, it is fitting to split the place, and drain pus; and cure it as we have said, until it be healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the hip is broken in this way, as with the shoulder and arm; however, in this restoration, the patient does not ring any bells.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the hip is restored in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the knee's vein
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the knee joint there are few fractures, but it bends many times.  
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, then it is no longer just a crack, or a puncture, and it becomes like every wound, and without wound, and this everyone knows well. 
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that one puts equal those who are rounded to their places, as long as it is assembled moves as one can; then put the splint, and put on it a round piece of wood, if you need it, and restrain it as it suits, then reward all the dispositions that we have said in other wounds, as hot abscesses and similar; so put to each accident what suits him, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, so one is called by right 'mustelz', and the other is called 'foscile'; and they have all the same fracture as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is like that of the arm equally, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in every way. 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is seen well; and it turns downwards. 
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore administer extension, and place it even, and bind the bones evenly; but nonetheless, if the fracture is bad, and there are many pieces, that the extension be minor and lighter; and the splint according to your strength. 
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two pieces of seasoned wood that support the leg on either side, and be long from the knee down to below; then wrap them in two layers with one bandage above and below, and tie it in the middle as well, and at this juncture, the leg cannot incline to the right or left, and thus it is good. And no one administers a single stick along the length of the leg, and if it is wood, it is placed on the leg to prevent movement, and properly done is this in the fracture where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or other accident; and cure thus until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there comes no fracture, but to the bones of the foot comes often fracture and at two points, and there happen only a few in more situations.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there happens fracture of the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, put the patient's foot on the ground, as if he would like to walk, and then put your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press them until they return into their places; then put the splint and bandages on, and put under the belly of the foot a small board to 2 finger spans wide, then restrain the foot with a bandage, then when you have wrapped the bandages and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when 3 or 4 days will have passed, untie the bandage, because you will find the bones aligned, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are some of the bones broken, restore them, as we have said for the bones of the hand; then put on the broken bone a splint according to the length of the bone, and be one finger more wide, then put under the foot that table that I have said, and restrain it well; and if there are .ij. or .iij., or more, broken, put on each bone a splint according to its quantity, enveloped in .i. cloth of linen, and restrain the table under the foot; and let it stand on the top of the table before the belly of the foot, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said to the other fractures, as we have said; and cure each accident as it is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the woman's nature is broken, make the sitting enlarged, then incline it to the part of the back, and let it be held by behind; then fill the basin of the woman with cotton, and put in as much as the stool; then turn the woman over, and lift her back little by little, and then jump the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of nature, and the bone returns with the stool; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and thus do for seven days or around: so will be restored the fracture, and if you see, take a sheep bladder, and tie a rope at one end, and put the whole bladder into nature; then blow into the rope firmly, until the bladder is inflated inside: nature will return the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it so for some days, until it is healed. 
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the finger of the man or of the woman is broken, restore it like as we have said in the bone of the hip; and are not concealed these fractures near him who puts his study and his use into it, and attends my book.  
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture, it signifies more than one way to restore it: then therefore. 
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the member, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and put it in the member; then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days or until healed, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is great, such as the bone of the hip or shoulder or similar, that he be healed now, so that the healings that we have said testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then retain the vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin to restore the fracture in that same hour or day, if no abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess comes to it, then let the restoration wait until the ninth day, until the abscess is appeased, and do not touch it for three days or four, because you would bring evil accidents upon it.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is appearing on the uncovered chest, then it befits that you put it lightly in its place with your hands, with small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not readily available to put it in place with your hands, then resort to this instrument which is of iron, which is .vij. or .viij. long, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this, it is necessary that the maker makes .iii. or iiij., according to what he needs in each cure of a fracture; and let it be round and a little thick, so that it does not bend under compression on the member during your work, and let it be tapered at the front, and thicker from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called “palainche,” for which the shoulder blade must be placed on top of the visible bone; and pull it at once, until it returns, and be equal to each other. 
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is fine, and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, then it is necessary that you break the head of the bone, as long as the instruments have hold. 
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument, either a knife or saw, to your power; then reinsert what remains in the bone of sharpness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. 
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If so long as it is in its place, then soak the drapery in black wine vinegar, and properly cleanse it when it is clean; and do not put on the wound any cerote nor anything else where there is oil, that it may not bring forth rot and corruption; then administer compresses when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut away the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and give heed well that the wound be not strained with the fracture; and many times have foolish people done this and brought upon the patient death or corrosion at any time; and let the strapping be softer and more supple than for other fractures.  
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident may come, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it does not behoove to put on stars; but wrap around, in place of stars, hard drapes, and tie them. 
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is beginning to swell, remove those things which you have placed on it and put healing ointment for wounds, such as ointment tetrafarmotion and similar. 
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you untie the limb two times a day, morning and evening, until it is joined and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be supported in such a manner that the bone fits together lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if this day passes, and it cannot be joined but returns into place, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which it is necessary that you cover the wound with a bandage, and remove all these loose pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or any other manner of corruption, then it is necessary that you cure it, according to what he says in his chapter before. 
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken, and open on the limb, such as the bone of the hip or the shoulder, and other similar bones of the large limbs, if you do not treat it, because many times death comes, but leave it until it decays; perchance it will heal by itself after XX days or XXX, then cure the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it. 
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of boils which come from the swelling
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	They often come after the health of the fracture, even when it's near the joint, and it is a bad thing to see the figure of the limb; and by chance cannot do the limbs its natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take ward therefore if it comes to us: if it administers topical medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acaice, and similar things, in the way that you take any of these things, or all together, and they confit with a stimulating wine or with yolk of egg or with honey; and put them on the knot in poultices, and hold it well, and do not untie it for days; and then untie it, and start another one, until the nodules are removed; or you strain onto a piece of plank well made; because the properties of the plank are that it removes all swelling from the limbs; and if the nodule is already converted into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, so cut above it, and make the superfluity appear; or you reapply it to any razor, until it is removed, and the cure as long as it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb that is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is restored, and afterwards the limb remains weak and thin, it happens for many reasons: one reason is because it was tied too tightly and not tied as it should; or because there were too many bandages and the member could not come back to its proper function; or because of excessive swelling; or because of too much movement, not at the right time; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat and make his body soft, as long as the blood is multiplied in him; and administer baths to him, and give him joy and pleasure; then put poultices on the limb so that the poultice attracts great movement, and the swelling often of water comes down, until the movement returns to the limb; and it returns to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The member twisted after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bones are apart, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function: so do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb all over again, and many foolish people have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and brings great harm, and perhaps death; however, if the knots and the torture are fresh, then it behooves them to be raised with hot water, or softening herbs are cooked, such as leaves of wormwood, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and the one i. make a softening plaster, such as diacoylon well made, and you take the poultice of wormwood, and confit it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top; or you take figs grease, and grind them with flaxseed, and similar medicines that lessen swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes is dislocation removed by rubbing continuously and lengthwise with moist hands. 
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And bring movement to the limb every hour. 
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is ingrained and hardened, like stone, and need be to remove it with iron, then it behoves to cut up to the bone, with a subtle and light incision; and put care and study into the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is from any joint out of its place, for which it cannot move, and the limb is poorly formed, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if it is now necessary to bring back without bracing.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the swelling increases, and by chance when it is reset, there is pain; for this reason it is not good to move it while it is swollen; many times it brings forth suppuration and other pains; however, when this happens, make the patient bleed, then leave it, until the abscesses are all quieted; then raise the member with hot water and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each member as the wound comes in its place. 
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens sometimes that the jaws become dislocated and the dislocations are in two ways: either they are a little bit out of their places and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the cheek, and close the saliva from the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and wraps his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by many more positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then it behooves you to reset it carefully, and do not hesitate; and in such a manner that the ministers hold the head of the patient, and puts his fingers into the root of the dislocation of the mandible inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other two hands should be outside, to put it straight; and command the patient to soften his mandibles, and move them in all directions. 
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the minister puts it equal, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is brought back (re-aligned) painfully, even if it is the two jaws together, apply hot water and oil, until they are gently moved; do not hesitate to bring it back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient is well closed with softened cloth, so put on top of cloths moistened in a cerote made of rose oil and wax, then tie it lightly with soft bandages; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his shoulders be between two cushions, so that he does not move them neither to the right nor to the left, nor does he try to eat, but takes light food, as long as the pains are gone, and the jaws are healed; and then chew what he wants lightly, and do not work at all to open the mouth for eating and drinking, as long as the jaw is well healed and sound. 
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be set in place within an hour, and are not returned to their places, then come fevers and accustomed swellings, and perhaps a belly ache, and perhaps vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a dangerous thing; and many times die those who have it, within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The harness cannot dislocate from within the side of the ribs and the hip, and it is dislocated no times outside, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies sound on his back, and extends his arms; and then press the place firmly with your palm, and it will return; then put on the splint and bandage, and restrain it; and the shoulder which is towards the outside cannot dislocate; if perhaps it does, and if it dislocates any time, restore it to its place, as we have said; then put on the splint and bandage, and restrain it, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus same is brought back the shoulder joint, when it is out of place. 
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: one of which is that it is dislocated to the part of the seat downward; and the second is to the part of the breast; and by chance it is dislocated to the upper part, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inside for the nerves; and many times dislocated down towards the seat, especially in those who have little flesh, because in these it is easily thrown; in those who have enough flesh, it is thrown with difficulty, and returns with difficulty. 
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps it happens to some men percussion or fracture, and swells the shoulder with a hot abscess, and thinks that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary that you feel it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the cure.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And is known the dislocations when it is pulled down towards the hip, and puts difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between their variety manifest; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and below the hip to touch the top of the shoulder, as if it were one piece; and the patient cannot bring back his hand to his side, nor move from any movement; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you find it manifestly at the touch; and this manner of dislocation is not only to be brought back, when it is new, or if the child is sick.  
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the ministers raise the hand of the sick person upwards, then put their fingers below the armpit, and raise the joint with force upward to its place; and the minister raises the hand, and extends it upwards, then puts it below; so it will come back gently.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in a few days after, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and administer ointment softening and soothing, such as decoction of aloe and fenugreek and melilot in water, and be administered; then be supported the patient on his back, and put under the buttocks a sto of wool equal, neither too soft nor too hard, then put the heel of the foot on the sto, and lift the head of the shoulder skillfully, and pull the hand of the sick man; and another minister holds the head of the sick man, so that he does not move down; this shoulder returns all now, and if you see it re-insert according to this manner: and it is that you make a present of the man who is bigger than the patient; and be straight towards the ribs, and put his shoulder under the buttocks of the patient, and lift the buttocks up, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister pulls the hand of the sick man down towards the belly. 
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he can put with him any heavy thing, and the dislocation returns now. 
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And reset it also in another manner: and is a long stick put in the earth, whose head be as much as the pillow, and not too big nor too thin; then be put under the sick person, but that he have coverings above, and the sick person be standing by the long of the shaft; then be stretched his hand down on the other side forming, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then make this cure: take a stick of II arms long and IIII fingers wide, which has the head rounded to enter easily under the armpit, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie above the head of the staff cloths so that the staff does not hurt the patient, then put it below the armpit of the patient; and extend his arm up on the staff's long side, and tie the shoulder to the staff, and the arm to the head of the hand, then put the arm on one step of a ladder wide, and let the hands be extended down, and let the body hang on the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, in whatever manner that it is, it behooves you to put under the strap a ball of wool even, then place the plaster of powdered mill, with incense and yolk saffron, on the whole shoulder and around, then strain it under the strap gently, and turn the linen on the plaster, and embrace the hand at its collar, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it behooves him to move little, as long as the limb is strengthened, for it will heal more quickly; and then move more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come or for another cause, then you must administer cautery to it in three punctures, as it is laid out in the chapter on cautery. 
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all these things, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift his arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation which is toward the hip, and the breasts, or behind, it is made by impulse, and stretching of hands, and there administer another place; and care until it be healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes pain in the limb, and slowness of movement, then make the patient take many baths, until that pain is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and at points returns; and if it has been dislocated from all sides, even in front and behind, and the dislocation is not restored, because one sees it well and feels it well; and dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the knife to the patient with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly. 
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all. 
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it thus as abscesses come to its aid, because if abscesses were to come to its aid, it would be grievous to bring it back; and perhaps it cannot be brought back completely at all, even when it is in the back; so it is worse than the other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and perhaps death comes from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is like this when it can be brought back that you extend his hand with your two hands; and his arms be spread, and the hands do move according to the knife around, above and below, and put the joint to its shoulders together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and hold of the root of the palm the knife which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and that two ministers extend the arm, and hold it with their hands, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side, then that you have enveloped a double long and wide cloth; and when the minister joins the joint with his hand, he puts oil on one of the oils to soften the joint, then pushes the joint together until it returns; and when it is in its place, put a dry plaster over it with honey from an egg, and hold it firmly, and place the arm at the collarbone of the sick person, and leave it for several days, then untie. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, she unties the bandage and leaves it; and if you see that the joint is not set well, she re-applies the plaster and the bandage, and leaves it like that for some days, until it is firmly set; then unties it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the joint has been reset, and it moves, bathe him and rub him well, and press until it is soothed; or you put on the joint a fleece of fat sheep, then leave it for one day and night, then remove it, and let it enter into the bath; and when it sweats, rub the joint moderately, then put the fleece back on, and then enter into the bath; and thus do it two or three times, until it is healed; and if you see, put on wool cloth moistened with warm butter, and strain it on; it will return to its place. 
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is easier than other joints. Nonetheless, it should be returned to its place immediately, as soon as it is dislocated, so that the place does not become inflamed or come to have a hot abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the putting back is that you put the sick hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and he places it equal, so that he puts his palm upon the appearance of the joint, and pushes it as much as it comes back all the way, it is necessary that you look if it is well in its place; then put the sick person's back of his hand on a table at the extension and putting back. 
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, put the patient's back of his hand on the table, and the mirror puts his hand on the appearance of the joint. 
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is good. If not, then the restraint of soothing plasters upon the abscess will be applied, and let it be left so until it restarts.  
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, the joint remains twisted; and does no harm to the patient other than as long as the hand is numb, and cannot pull anything at all: therefore know that the nerve is cut, or the artery; so there is no other means except to constrain by cautery according to the case, and perhaps there is nothing else of value. 
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put it on the splint that we have said, then strap it and leave it for 5 days, then untie it and leave it so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no wound, then moisten it with hot water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	No times are dislocated the bones of the hand on each side, no times on the back of the palm or the belly; therefore are the bones and put the dislocation to your pouches until it returns, then sustain the chief of the bone, and the pent towards the part where it is disjoined; and let him 2 days, and then puts him equal that day; and don’t tie it, as we have said, and unties it every day, and makes it move, and ties it again; and do this often, until it is straight, and all also do, if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and all also do, when it is dislocated on other part. 
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of dislocation of the shoulder blade of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade of the back or the neck is dislocated, or there are many dislocations, if there is no cure, because death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs of this are that the joints jump forth without will, and cannot be held, and many times they soften any limb, or the two hips or the two arms or one. 
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or percussion or similar things, the ancients said manners of cures by great words, in which there is no great profit at all; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways. 
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gibbosity which comes to the breast in front, there is nothing nor cure; and also the one which comes straight into II costs, and it cannot be cured except the one properly which comes to the back, as I said; and it is that the patient should be stretched on his face in the same place, and have strain below him, so that he does not move; then put the splint at the head in the earth forming, and the other to the feet, and tie a rope below the shoulders of the patient, and the other to the hips, and knees, and ankles; and two ministers grasp the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the II splints; and be well bound, the splint as we have said, and the mire puts his palms on the spine forming, until it returns. 
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, then take a board three arms long, and place it beneath the arm pit, and have the patient lie on his side, and put the head of the board under the armpit, then place the middle of the board upon the spine; and place the patient's feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do it to the turner who turns by hand. 
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And that you place II splints on the head of the patient's arm of a large, and towards the feet II others, and there be between each splint, outside and inside, a palm's width of long; and have in each splint I hole, where the rope goes through, and let the splints be firmly in earth so that they do not move; and between each II splints have I turning splint, on which the ropes turn, and have in II turning splints II small splints of a palm's width, for to turn the turn; and then tie the rope which is among the shackles to the turn towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other turn, and each of the ministers turns his turn all over the rope, and the master puts the spine equal as we have said. 
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.
