And when it is even, put a drying plaster with an abundance of egg, and then the compresses, and then the splint of a tablet of III thumbs in length, that presses the place of the rib and the part of the spine from below, then tie it with a linen, as we have said, and use the patient to subtle nourishment, until he is healed; and if any thing comes at the end of the healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the splint that we have said before; and sometimes one administers a piece of wood, and sometimes it appears in the back vertebra of the back, and one thinks that it is dislocation; and this is the bone which opens, for that reason one must not have presumption; by chance would bring death. 
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come out as dislocations, not like other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated in .iiij. parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside then, and little dislocated front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens more the diseased knee than the healthy one, and the diseased one cannot bend his knee; and there is the swelling which is below inflamed with a hot abscess, because the head of the hip comes there. 
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes to fire, so is this accident contrary to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of him to whom it comes to the front, so is that he is well his leg according to the fulfillment; however, do not double the knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot before, and holds back his urine, and swells the groin, and when he goes, he passes above the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of him to whom it comes behind, so is that he cannot expand his knee, nor double, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the groin is softened, and is the head of the hip at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The return of this kind of dislocation is that you should consider if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its arrangement, so there is no cure; and it does not behoove him at all that he has presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those whose dislocation is fresh, and there are .iiij. manners of dislocation, so hurry that you return the joint, and the extension inside and outside, and the movement to right and left; perhaps it will return, and there is no need for other care.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then it is necessary that you appear with a strong minister, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or on the loin that is tied above the knee; and another minister stretches his hand upwards in such a way that he pushes his hands below his shoulders, then tightens with a sudden force above the hip; and another holds the head of the thigh; and extend it both up and down at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging. 
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four similar things, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this is not so, it is necessary to take care of its appearance When the dislocation is at the shoulder, it is necessary that you support the patient on his healthy side, then place the linen on the root of the hip, and the place which is below the groin, then extend the linen upwards towards the groin, and towards the thigh; then seize some other ministers his arms, and embrace the large part of the diseased hip, and stretch it outwards in a firm manner; now it will return to its place; and this kind of dislocation is lighter than others. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the sick person together with a strong linen cord above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the diseased leg be extended two spans more than the other; then let it be hung by the head from a pole, and let it be two arms' length above the ground; then command the minister to embrace the head of the hip, and let other ministers standing with the sick person, who firmly embrace the hip, because the joint now returns readily.  
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is on the outside, so the patient lies down, as we have said in the one who has gilbosite, and restrain the loin upon the leg sick properly, and upon the hip also; then put II tisons, I to the head and I other to the feet, then stick I tison between the hips of the patient in the form; and ait plantei of drapelz moist entor, that it does not blister the sick one, then extend each minister towards him, and the mines puts equal to his hand the dislocation. 
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good. 
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If this is not so, put him on a table, and press him as we have said in the glossary, and lie the patient on his healthy side. 
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the sick leg as far as possible, and according to what I have said; and put the minister's pain on the sick ankle, then press with the other hand, and bring it down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the hip, it is not necessary to stretch the patient down, nor raise up the land, but it should be as if the hip had been dislocated outward, as we have said about the lying of the two hips; and let it be on its face, and the band stretched as we have said before, and one must press upon the joint at the table; and it will be good when the patient stretches his legs, and they are equal; therefore adjust the thighs, and put the splint, and the strap of a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and let him rest for three days or four, then undo it, and put the splint on top; and if you see that they are equal, then strap them as before, and leave it for three days; then undo it, and let him walk well, until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg to his hip, and if he does not rest on his hip, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his flank, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and retract between your two hands, then bend the two bones that form the knee; and other ministers extend his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he rests his leg on his hip lightly; and put the plaster on top, and make the leg rest on the hip, and tie them together firmly for three days or four, then untie it; and do not let the patient move, as long as the limb is strengthened. 
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, administer strong stretching, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.  
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels is sometimes dislocated, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs of this are that the ankle is swollen, and tender before the part where it is dislocated; the reduction of this is light, and one should extend it gently with his hands when it is only bruised. 
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated completely, it behooves you to make the patient sit straight, and hold him by the ministers except by the leg, above the ankle; then pull the foot toward you with your right hand, and then with your left two times, then raise it upwards, and gently push the foot upward; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, it is well; if not, begin the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and put a stake firmly in the ground between his hips, and tie drapes around it so that it does not move the patient; then hold the ministers by the hip, and other ministers extend the foot to their hands or at the ligament, so that they tie it above the ankle of the foot; then extend each minister equally, and the stakes be firm between the hips of the patient to retain the patient when one is raising; then put the ministers equally the dislocation in their hands, and other ministers hold the sound leg below, and the dislocation will return readily.   
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is pointed, put the plaster and dressings on top, and strain them firmly, and tie the leg to the leg, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the ligatures are not too tight; then leave him for II days or III, and if the ligatures soften, then strain them again; then untie it on the third day or fourth, and forbid the patient from walking for IIII days; and if he goes before this time limit, it is not certain that he will not dislocate again. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes from there, then it is necessary that you appease it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the hips are dislocated, it is necessary to gently extend them without effort, and it is an easy thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back or foot, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a level place or on a table very straight, and put your foot on what opens of these joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it returns; and when it is equal, and there is nothing open, then put under the sole of the foot a table at the shoulder, then strain it firmly, and let it remain for III days, then untie it; and make him rest, until he is healed.  
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and you want to restore it, many times the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and tardy, nor rash; and use at the beginning of things soothing apoplexy hot, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the apoplexy may be on it; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing apoplexy hot, and cure the wound, as it is proper, with dried ointments; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are dislocated, then set the bones, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and guard yourself from entering into the way of fear, according to what I have said, for this will cost you death according to your Creator, and for the safety of your arm and your body.  
Amen	So be it
